Recovery from Excuse Revives Original Obligation
Ruling when the excuse ends within the ila' period

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a husband's excuse ends during the ila' period and explain why verbal fi'a becomes void and intercourse is required.

Core Idea
A substitute (verbal fi'a) ceases when the excuse ends; the original obligation (intercourse) revives.

In the previous lesson, we learned that a husband unable to have intercourse may return from ila' verbally. But what happens if his excuse disappears before the four-month period expires? This lesson examines a critical scenario where the substitute ruling collapses and the original method becomes mandatory. The ruling underscores a key Hanafi principle: primacy of the original act over a temporary concession.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scenario
The husband had made ila' (swore to abstain from intercourse for four months). Due to an excuse (e.g., illness), he made a verbal declaration of return (verbal fi'a). The excuse then ends before the four months expire.
This is a change in circumstance.
2
Identify the Initial Ruling
Verbal fi'a was initially valid because the husband was unable to have intercourse. The ruling is based on necessity (darura).
Necessity permits the substitute.
3
Identify the Change and New Ruling
Once the excuse ends, the verbal fi'a becomes batil (void). The husband must now have intercourse to return from ila'.
The original obligation revives when the impediment is removed.
4
State the Dalil
The proof is the impact (athar) from Ibn Abbas: 'Al-fay' al-jima' (the return is intercourse). This establishes that intercourse is the essential method.
This is a hadith ahad, but its meaning is clear (qat'i dalala).
5
Understand the Principle
The ruling is based on the legal maxim: 'When the original becomes possible, the substitute ceases.' Verbal fi'a is a temporary concession, not a permanent alternative.
This principle appears in other areas of fiqh as well.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[ ۲۰۰۰) (۱۱) اور اگر تندرست ہو گیا مدت میں تو باطل ہو جائے گا یہ رجوع اور ہو جائے گا اس کا رجوع جماع کرنا۔
الری عذر کی بنا پر زبان سے رجوع کر لیا تھا۔ لیکن ابھی چار مہینے گزرنے سے پہلے عذر ختم ہو گیا اور جماع پر قادر ہو گیا تو اب جماع کر کے ہی رجوع کرنا ہوگا۔
ایلاء سے رجوع کرنے کے لئے جماع کرنا ضروری ہے اور وہی اصل ہے۔ اور زبان سے رجوع کرنا فرع ہے اور مجبوری کی بنیاد پر ہے۔ اس لیئے جب اصل پر قادر ہو گیا تو اصل یعنی جماع ہی سے رجوع کرنا ہو گا (۲) اثر میں ہے۔ عن ابن عباس قال الفيء الجماع (ب) (سنن للبیہقی ، باب الفدية الجماع الامن عذرج سابع ، ص ۶۲۴ نمبر ۱۵۲۳۴ مصنف عبدالرزاق ، باب الفی الجماع ج سادس ص ۴۶۱ نمبر ۱۱۶۷۴ار مصنف ابن ابی هیبته ۱۲۹ من قال لا فی الہ الا الجماع ج رابع ، ص ۱۳۶، نمبر ۱۸۵۹۵) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ رجوع کا اصل طریقہ جماع ہی ہے۔ اس لئے مدت ایلاء میں جماع پر قدرت ہو جائے تو جماع کر کے رجوع کرنا ہوگا۔
[2000] (11) And if he becomes healthy within the period, then that return becomes invalid, and his return must be by intercourse. He had made a verbal return due to an excuse. But before four months had passed, the excuse ended and he became able to have intercourse, so now he must return by intercourse. For returning from ila', intercourse is necessary, and it is the original. Verbal return is secondary and based on necessity. Therefore, when he becomes able to do the original, he must return by intercourse. (2) There is an impact: from Ibn Abbas, he said: 'The return (fi'a) is intercourse.' (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, etc.) From this impact, it is known that the original method of return is intercourse. So if he becomes able to have intercourse during the ila' period, he must return by intercourse.

Commentary
This lesson follows logically from the previous one. If a husband had made a verbal fi'a because he was unable to have intercourse (due to sickness, distance, etc.), but then his excuse ends before the four-month period expires, the verbal fi'a becomes null and void. He must now actually consummate the marriage. The principle is that the primary method of returning from ila' is intercourse; verbal declaration is a temporary substitute for hardship. When the hardship is removed, the substitute ceases, and the original obligation revives. The proof is from the statement of Ibn Abbas: 'The return is intercourse.' This underscores that verbal fi'a is not a permanent alternative but a concession for necessity.

Key Terms
الفيء الجماع (al-fay’ al-jimāʿ): The fundamental way to return from ila' is through sexual intercourse.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) He must make another verbal fi'a
C) He must have intercourse
D) The ila' period extends automatically

Key Takeaway
The substitute (verbal fi'a) is contingent on the excuse; removing the excuse revives the original obligation of intercourse.

Saying 'You are Haram' – Probing Intention
Ruling on ambiguous declaration of 'haram'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the ambiguous phrase 'You are haram to me' and explain why the husband's intention must be investigated.

Core Idea
When a husband says 'You are haram', his intention determines the legal effect – it is not a direct divorce.

The word 'haram' (forbidden) is ambiguous in Islamic law. When a husband uses it toward his wife, it could mean divorce, zihar, ila', or a mere oath. The Hanafi school requires us to ask the husband about his intention before assigning a ruling. This lesson explores that principle and the proof from the Companion Ibn Mas'ud.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ambiguous statement
The phrase 'You are haram to me' (anti 'alayya haram) is legally ambiguous – it can imply multiple rulings.
In other schools, it might be a direct divorce, but Hanafis treat it as multi-interpretable.
2
Apply the rule of intention (niyya)
According to the Hanafi school, the husband must be asked what he intended. His answer determines whether it is divorce, ila', zihar, or an oath.
If he intended ila', the rules of ila' apply; if he intended divorce, then divorce takes effect.
3
Examine the proof (dalil)
The text cites an athar (tradition) from Ibn Mas'ud regarding ila' – when a man who has sworn to abstain from intercourse cannot physically perform it, his verbal return (fi'a) is sufficient. This shows that intention and circumstance matter.
The athar is used analogically to support probing intention in the 'haram' case.
4
Note the cross-madhhab difference
The Shafi'i school often treats 'haram' as a direct divorce without investigating intention. The practical consequence (thamarah) is that in the Hanafi school a divorce may not occur if the husband intended something else.
This difference is legitimate ikhtilaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
۲۰۰۱ (۱۲) واذا قال لامرأته انت على حرام سئل عن نيته فان قال اردت [ ا سے کہہ دے کہ میں نے بیوی سے رجوع کر لیا تو اس کہہ دینے سے ایلاء ساقط ہو جائے گا اور قسم کا کفارہ لازم ہوگا۔ البتہ اگر جماع پر قادر ہو تو جماع کرنے سے ہی ایلاء ساقط ہوگا۔
اس اثر میں اس کا ثبوت ہے۔ وقال ابن مسعود فان كان به علة من كبر او مرض او حبس يحول بينه وبين الجماع فان فيشه ان يفيء بقلبه او لسانه (الف) (مصنف ابن ابی هیته ۲۹ امن قال لافی الہ الا الجماع ج رابع ص ۱۳۶، نمبر ۱۸۶۰۲ اسفن للبیہقی ، باب الفیة الجماع الا من عذرج سابع ص ۶۲۴ نمبر ۱۵۲۳۵ مصنف عبدالرزاق ، باب الفی الجماع ج سادس ص ۴۶۲ نمبر ۱۱۶۷۷)

2001 (12) And if he says to his wife 'You are haram to me', he is asked about his intention. If he said 'I intended...' [then the ruling follows]. He says: 'I have returned to my wife.' Then by that saying, ila' drops and expiation for the oath becomes obligatory. However, if he is able to have intercourse, ila' drops only by intercourse. There is evidence in this athar: Ibn Mas'ud said: if there is an excuse such as old age, sickness, or imprisonment that prevents intercourse, then his fi'a is to return with his heart or tongue. From this athar, it is known that if there is an excuse, verbal return is sufficient and ila' drops. Ratta': a woman with blocked vagina. Fi'a: return from ila'.

Commentary
This lesson deals with the ambiguous phrase 'You are haram to me' (anti 'alayya haram). The Hanafi approach is to ask the husband about his intention because the word 'haram' can imply several things: it could be a declaration of divorce (ba'in or mughalladha), zihar, ila', or simply an oath. If he intended ila', then it is treated as such. The ruling also reiterates the earlier point about verbal fi'a being valid when intercourse is impossible, but if possible, intercourse is required. The text here appears to combine the ruling on the ambiguous phrase with a repetition of the earlier athar from Ibn Mas'ud, possibly due to the OCR. The key point is the emphasis on intention (niyya) to determine the legal effect.

Key Terms
حرام (ḥarām): Literally 'forbidden'; when said to a wife, it is ambiguous and can mean multiple legal acts.
إيلاء (īlā’): A vow by a husband to abstain from sexual intercourse with his wife for a period of four months or more.

Key Takeaway

Verbal Return (Fi' bi-l-Lisan) in Ila' When Excused
Explains method of returning to wife during Ila' when unable to consummate

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on fi' when the husband is excused and apply the condition that verbal return becomes invalid if the excuse ends within the period.

Core Idea
When unable to consummate, a verbal declaration of return is valid, but only as long as the excuse lasts — if ability returns, only intercourse suffices.

This passage addresses a specific concession in Ila': the husband who has sworn an oath to abstain from intercourse may return to his wife verbally if he is physically unable to consummate. However, this substitute operates only during the excuse. The text provides the ruling, the condition, and the sahabi evidence. Understanding this nuance prevents the common error of assuming verbal fi' is always sufficient.

Guided Path
1
Identify the default ruling for fi'
Understand that the primary act of return (fi') is sexual intercourse. This is the original rule (asl) from which the exception arises.
The passage cites Ibn Abbas: 'al-fay'u al-jima'' (the return is intercourse).
2
Identify the valid excuse
Recognize what constitutes a valid excuse: old age, illness, imprisonment, or distance that prevents access to the wife during the Ila' period.
The excuse must be genuine and total; temporary or partial inability may not qualify.
3
State the substitute ruling
When the husband is excused, he may return simply by saying 'I have returned to you' (or equivalent) with the intention of returning.
This verbal declaration suffices to drop the Ila' and avoids the automatic divorce.
4
Apply the condition of duration
If the excuse ends within the four-month period (e.g., he recovers from illness), the earlier verbal return becomes void, and he must now perform intercourse to effect a valid return.
The ruling returns to the original principle: intercourse is the only valid fi' when ability exists.
5
Locate the evidence
The passage relies on the athar of Ibn Mas'ud: 'If there is a disability ... his return is that he returns with his heart or tongue.'
This is a mursal hadith (sahabi statement) with zanni thubut and dalala, but accepted in Hanafi fiqh.

Source Text

If there was a distance between them that he cannot reach her during the period of Ila', then his return (fi') is that he says with his tongue: 'I have returned to her.' If he says that, the Ila' is dropped. And if he becomes well in the period, that return becomes invalid and his return is intercourse. And if he says to his wife 'You are haram upon me', he is asked about his intention; if he says 'I intended falsehood', it is as he said. ... (Urdu commentary follows) The evidence for this is the narration: Ibn Mas'ud said, 'If there is a disability of old age, illness, or imprisonment that prevents him from intercourse, then his return is that he returns with his heart or tongue.' From this narration it is understood that if there is an excuse, returning verbally is sufficient and the Ila' is dropped. ... And if he becomes healthy within the period, this return becomes invalid and his return is intercourse. ... The effect is: Ibn Abbas said, 'The return (fi') is intercourse.' From this narration it is understood that the original method of return is intercourse. Therefore, if he becomes able to have intercourse during the period of Ila', he must return by intercourse.
Source pages p. 146

Commentary
This passage begins a new sub-chapter on the method of fi' (return) in Ila'. The ruling is clear: the default method of returning to one's wife after swearing an oath of Ila' is through actual sexual intercourse. However, if there is a valid excuse—such as distance, old age, illness, or imprisonment that prevents intercourse—the husband may return simply by declaring verbally, 'I have returned to you.' This verbal declaration suffices because the inability to perform the primary act (intercourse) shifts the obligation to its substitute, just as tayammum substitutes for wudu when water is unavailable. The commentator cites the authority of Ibn Mas'ud to support this concession. Importantly, if the excuse ends during the four-month period (e.g., the husband recovers from illness), the earlier verbal return becomes void, and he must now perform actual intercourse to effect a valid return. The ruling is based on the principle that the original (asl) is intercourse, and verbal return is merely a branch (far') that operates only in necessity. When the necessity ceases, the original ruling resumes. This is further confirmed by the narration from Ibn Abbas stating that 'fi' is intercourse.'

Key Terms
الإيلاء (al-ila'): An oath sworn by a husband to abstain from sexual intercourse with his wife for a period of four months or more. In Hanafi fiqh, if he does not return within four months, a single revocable divorce occurs automatically.
الفيء (al-fay'): The act of returning to one's wife during the Ila' period. In Hanafi fiqh, it is primarily by intercourse, but by verbal declaration when excused.
العذر (al-'udhr): A valid excuse that prevents the husband from performing intercourse, such as old age, illness, or imprisonment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
During Ila', a husband becomes ill and cannot have intercourse. He says, 'I have returned to you.' Then he recovers before four months pass. What is the ruling on his return?
A) His verbal return is valid and the Ila' is dropped permanently.
B) His verbal return becomes invalid when he recovers, and he must now return by intercourse.
C) His verbal return is never valid; only intercourse counts as return.
D) He must repeat the verbal return after recovery to keep the Ila' dropped.

Key Takeaway
Verbal fi' is a valid substitute for intercourse only when the husband has a valid excuse and only for the duration of that excuse.

The Legal Effect of 'Anti 'Ala Haram' According to Intention
Rulings and proofs for the phrase 'haram' with various intentions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the five possible intentions for the phrase 'anti 'ala haram' and derive the corresponding ruling for each intention, citing the Hanafi proofs (Qur'an and athar).

Core Idea
The word 'haram' is a kinaya—its legal effect depends entirely on the speaker's intention.

In Hanafi fiqh, the phrase 'anti 'ala haram' does not automatically effect divorce. Instead, it is an allusive expression (kinaya) whose outcome is determined by the speaker's actual intention. This passage lays out five possible intentions—lying, divorce, zihar, prohibition, or no intention—and provides the ruling and proofs for each. Understanding this principle is essential for correctly applying the law in cases of marital disputes involving such ambiguous statements.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the phrase as kinaya
Identify that 'haram' is an allusive word (kinaya) in Hanafi fiqh, meaning its legal effect is not fixed but depends on the speaker's intention.
Unlike sarih (explicit) words for divorce, kinaya requires niyyah (intention) to produce a legal effect.
2
Enumerate the five categories of intention
List the five possible intentions mentioned in the text: lying, divorce, zihar, prohibition (tahrim), and no intention. Note that each yields a different ruling.
These are not exhaustive but cover the common possibilities.
3
Extract the ruling and proof for each intention
For each category, read the passage to find the ruling (e.g., no effect for lying, one ba'in talaq for divorce, zihar for zihar intention, oath for prohibition/no intention) and the proof cited (athar from Thawri, Ibn Abbas, etc., or the Quranic verse).
Pay attention to how the proofs support the rulings.
4
Synthesize the overall principle
Conclude that the phrase alone is ambiguous; its legal outcome is determined by the speaker's intention. This shows the Hanafi emphasis on niyyah in marital and oath matters.
This principle is a key distinction from some other madhahib.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

كتاب الايلاء

الكذب فهو كما قال [ ۲۰۰۲ (۱۳) وان قال اردت به الطلاق فهي تطليقة بائنة الا ان ينوى الثلاث [ ۲۰۰۳ ۱۴ وان قال اردت به الظهار فهو ظهار

اس لئے یہ پوچھا جائے گا کہ حرام بول کر نیت کیا کی ہے؟ اس اعتبار سے فیصلہ ہوگا۔ اس لئے اگر اس نے جھوٹ بولنے کی نیت کی تو جھوٹ شمار کریں گے، اور عورت پر طلاق واقع نہیں ہوگی۔ (1) بیوی حقیقت میں حرام تو نہیں ہے وہ تو حلال ہے اس لئے واقعی وہ جھوٹ ہی بول رہا ہے۔ اور چونکہ نیت بھی جھوٹ کی کی ہے اس لئے اسی پر محمول کر کے طلاق واقع نہیں کریں گے (۲) اثر میں ہے۔ عن الثوري قال يقول في الحرام على ثلاثة وجوه ، ان نوى طلاقا فهو على مانوي، وان نوى ثلاثا فثلاث، وان نوى واحدة فواحدة بائنة، وان نوى يمينا فهي يمين، وان نوى لم ينو شيئا فهي كذبة فليس فيه كفارة (الف) (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب الحرام ج سادس ص ۴۰۵ نمبر ۱۱۳۹۰ار مصنف ابن ابی شبیه ۶۹ من قال الحرام یمین ولیست بطلاق ج رابع ، ص ۹۹ نمبر ۱۸۱۸۳) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ حرام بول کر جھوٹ کی نیت کرے تو کچھ واقع نہیں ہوگی۔ (۲۰۰۲) (۱۳) اور اگر کہا اس سے طلاق کی نیت کی تو ایک طلاق بائنہ ہوگی مگر یہ کہ نیت کرے تین ۔ تشریح انت علی حرام کہہ کر طلاق کی نیت کی تو کم سے کم ایک طلاق بائنہ واقع ہوگی۔ اور اگر تین طلاق کی نیت کی تو تین طلاقیں واقع ہوں گی۔ (۱) لفظ حرام کنایات میں سے ہے۔ اور کنایہ میں کم سے کم ایک طلاق بائن واقع ہوتی ہے۔ اور اگر تین کی نیت کرے تو تین بھی واقع ہوتی ہے (۲) او پر حضرت ثوری کا اثر گزرا جس میں تھا کہ ایک طلاق بائنہ واقع ہوگی اور تین کی نیت کی تو تین واقع ہوگی (۳) عن علی وزید بن ثابت في البرية والبتة والحرام انها ثلاث ثلاث (ب) (سن ليبقى ، باب من قال لامرأته انت على حرام ج سابع ج ۵۷۶، نمبر ۱۵۰۶۷) (۴) وقال الحسن نيته وقال اهل العلم اذا طلق ثلاثا فقد حرمت عليه حراما بالطلاق والفراق (ج) ( بخاری شریف، باب من قال لامرأته انت علی حرام ص ۷۹۲ نمبر ۵۲۶۴) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ نیت کرے تو تین طلاقیں واقع ہوں گی۔ ۲۰۰۳) (۱۴) اور اگر کہے کہ میں نے اس سے ظہار کی نیت کی تو ظہار ہوگا۔ انت علی حرام بول کر ظہار کرنے کی نیت کی تو بیوی سے ظہار واقع ہو جائے گا۔ اثر میں ہے۔ عن سماک بن الفضل عن وهب قالوا هو بمنزلة الظهار اذا قال هى على حرام عتق رقبة او صيام شهرين متتابعين او اطعام ستين مسكينا (۱) (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب الحرام ج سادس ص ۴۰۴ نمبر ۷ ۱۱۳۸) اس اثر میں ہے کہ حاشیہ : (الف) حضرت ثوری نے فرمایا حرام میں تین طریقے ہیں۔ اگر نیت کی طلاق کی تو جیسی نیت کی ویسی ہوگی۔ اور اگر نیت کی تین کی تو تین واقع ہونگی ۔ اور اگر نیت کی ایک کی تو ایک بائنہ واقع ہوگی۔ اور اگر نیت کی قسم کی تو قسم ہوگی۔ اور اگر کچھ نیت نہیں کی تو جھوٹ ہوگا۔ پس اس میں کفارہ نہیں ہوگا ( ب ) حضرت علی اور زید بن ثابت نے فرمایا کہ بریہ اور حرام میں تین تین طلاقیں واقع ہوں گی (ج) حضرت حسن فرماتے ہیں کہ نیت کا اعتبار ہے۔ اور اہل علم نے فرمایا اگر تین طلاقیں دے تو شوہر پر حرام ہو جائے گی اس لئے اس کو حرام کہتے ہیں طلاق اور فراق کی وجہ سے (د) حضرت وہب نے فرمایا لفظ حرام ظہار کے درجے میں ہے (باقی اگلے صفحہ پر )

ثم [ ۲۰۰۴] (۱۵) وان قال اردت به التحريم او لم ارد به شيئا فهى يمين يصير به موليا . حرام کے لفظ سے ظہار واقع ہوگا۔ [ ۲۰۰۴] (۱۵) اور اگر کہا میں نے اس سے حرمت کا ارادہ کیا ہے، یا کچھ ارادہ نہیں کیا تو یہ تم ہوگی اور اس سے ایلاء کرنے والا ہوگا۔ اگر طلاق کی نیت نہیں کی ، ظہار کی نیت بھی نہیں کی۔ اور جھوٹ بولنے کی بھی نیت نہیں کی بلکہ تحریم کی نیت یعنی حرام کرنے کی نیت کی ۔ یا کسی چیز کی بھی نیت نہیں کی تو ان دونوں صورتوں میں لفظ حرام سے قسم ہوگی اور ایلا بھی ہو جائے گا۔ حضور نے کچھ بیویوں کو حرام کیا جس سے تم واقع ہوئی اور کفارہ لازم ہوا۔ یا ایھا النبي لم تحرم ما احل الله لك تبتغى مرضات ازواجك والله غفور رحیم قل فرض الله لكم تحله ایمانکم (الف) ( آیت ۲ سورۃ التحریم ۶۶) اس آیت میں تحرم سے قسم ثابت ہوئی اور تحلہ ایمانکم سے قسم کا کفارہ دینے کی طرف اشارہ ہے (۲) ان ابن عباس قال في الحرام يكفر (ب) ( بخاری شریف ، سورۃ التحریم ، کتاب التفسیر ص ۷۲۹ نمبر ۴۹۱۱ر مسلم شریف ، وجوب الكفارة على من حرم امر انته ولم مینوی الطلاق ص ۴۷۸ نمبر ۱۴۷۳ سفن اللبیبی ، باب من قال لامرأته انت على حرام ج سابع میں ۵۷۴، نمبر ۱۵۰۵۶/ مصنف عبدالرزاق ، باب الحرام ج سادس ص ۴۰۰ نمبر ۱۱۳۶۱ار مصنف ابن ابی هیتة 49 من قال الحرام یمین ولیس بطلاق ج رابع ، ص ۹۹ نمبر ۱۸۱۸۳) (۳) عن ابن مسعود انه كان يـقـول نيته في الحرام مانوى ان لم يكن نوى طلاق فهي يمين (ج) (سن للبیہقی ، باب من قال لا مرانه انت على حرام ج سابع ، ص ۵۷۵، نمبر ۱۵۰۶۲ مصنف عبدالرزاق نمبر ۱۱۳۶۶) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ حرام میں کچھ نیت نہ کرے تو قسم واقع ہوگی ۔ اور قسم ہوگی تو ایلاء بھی ہوگا۔

حاشیہ : ( پچھلے صفحہ سے آگے ) جب کہ کہے وہ مجھ پر حرام ہے۔ اس لئے غلام آزاد کرے، یا پے در پے دو ماہ روزے رکھے یا ساٹھ مسکین کو کھانا کھلائے (الف)اے نبی کیوں حرام کرتے ہیں ایسی چیز کو جس کو اللہ نے حلال کی ہے بیویوں کی رضامندی کے لئے ۔ اور اللہ معاف کرنے والا اور رحم کرنے والا ہے۔ اللہ نے فرض کیا تمہارے لئے قسموں کو حلال کرنے کے لئے (ب) حضرت ابن عباس فرماتے ہیں کہ لفظ حرام میں کفارہ دے (ج) حضرت ابن مسعود فرماتے تھے لفظ حرام میں نیست کا اعتبار ہے جو بھی نیت کرے۔ اور اگر طلاق کی نیت نہ کرے تو قسم واقع ہوگی۔
The Sharh al-Thamiri, Part Three, Book of Ila'. The lie is as he said. [2002] (13) And if he said, 'I intended divorce by it,' then it is one irrevocable divorce unless he intended three. [2003] (14) And if he said, 'I intended zihar by it,' then it is zihar. So it will be asked: what did he intend by saying 'haram'? The ruling will be based on that. Therefore, if he intended lying, it will be considered a lie, and no divorce will occur on the wife. (1) The wife is not actually haram, she is halal, so he is indeed lying. And since his intention was lying, it will be interpreted accordingly and divorce will not occur. (2) There is an athar: From al-Thawri, he said: 'One says regarding haram in three ways: if he intended divorce, then it is according to his intention; if he intended three, then three; if he intended one, then one irrevocable; if he intended an oath, then it is an oath; if he intended nothing, then it is a lie and there is no kaffarah in it.' (Mussannaf Abd al-Razzaq, Bab al-Haram, vol. 6, p. 405, no. 11390; Mussannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, no. 69: 'Whoever said al-haram is an oath and not divorce', vol. 4, p. 99, no. 18183). From this athar it is known that if one says haram and intends a lie, nothing occurs. (2002) (13) And if he said he intended divorce by it, one irrevocable divorce occurs unless he intended three. Explanation: If he says 'anti 'ala haram' and intends divorce, at least one irrevocable divorce occurs. And if he intended three, three occur. (1) The word haram is among kinayat (allusive words). In kinayah, at least one irrevocable divorce occurs. And if he intends three, three also occur. (2) The athar of Thawri passed earlier that one irrevocable divorce occurs and if he intends three, three occur. (3) From Ali and Zayd bin Thabit: 'In al-bariyyah, al-battah, and al-haram, they are three, three.' (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, Bab man qala li-imra'atihi anti 'ala haram, vol. 7, p. 576, no. 15067). (4) Al-Hasan said: 'His intention (matters).' And the people of knowledge said: 'If he gives three divorces, then she becomes haram for him (i.e., unlawful) due to divorce and separation.' (Sahih al-Bukhari, Bab man qala li-imra'atihi anti 'ala haram, p. 792, no. 5264). From this athar it is known that if he intends, three divorces occur. (2003) (14) And if he says that he intended zihar by it, then it is zihar. If he says 'anti 'ala haram' with the intention of zihar, then zihar occurs from his wife. There is an athar: From Simak bin al-Fadl from Wahb, they said: 'It is in the position of zihar: if he says, "she is haram on me," (he must) free a slave, or fast two consecutive months, or feed sixty poor persons.' (Mussannaf Abd al-Razzaq, Bab al-Haram, vol. 6, p. 404, no. 11387). In this athar it is that (footnote): (a) Thawri said: In haram there are three ways: if he intended divorce, then as he intended; if he intended three, then three; if he intended one, then one irrevocable; if he intended an oath, then an oath; and if he intended nothing, then it is a lie, so there is no kaffarah in it. (b) Ali and Zayd bin Thabit said: In bariyyah and haram, three divorces occur. (c) Al-Hasan says: Intention is considered. And the people of knowledge said: If he gives three divorces, then the husband becomes haram for her, so it is called haram due to divorce and separation. (d) Wahb said: The word haram is in the rank of zihar. (Continued on next page.) Then [2004] (15) And if he said, 'I intended prohibition by it,' or 'I did not intend anything,' then it is an oath and he becomes an mu'li (one who takes ila'). The word haram gives zihar. [2004] (15) And if he said, 'I intended prohibition by it,' or 'I did not intend anything,' then it is a vow (yamin) and he becomes an mu'li from it. If he did not intend divorce, nor did he intend zihar, nor did he intend lying, but rather intended prohibition (tahrim) i.e., making unlawful, or did not intend anything, then in both cases the word haram is an oath and ila' will occur. The Prophet (ﷺ) made some of his wives haram, which resulted in an oath and kaffarah became obligatory. (Ayat 2 of Surah Tahrim 66): 'O Prophet, why do you forbid what Allah has made lawful to you, seeking the pleasure of your wives? And Allah is Forgiving and Merciful. Allah has already ordained for you the dissolution of your oaths.' In this verse, 'tuharrim' establishes an oath and 'tahlil aymanikum' indicates giving kaffarah for the oath. (2) Ibn Abbas said regarding 'haram': 'He must give kaffarah.' (Sahih al-Bukhari, Surah al-Tahrim, Kitab al-Tafsir, p. 729, no. 4911; Sahih Muslim, Wujub al-kaffarah 'ala man harrama imra'atahu wa lam yanwi al-talaq, p. 478, no. 1473; Sunan al-Bayhaqi, Bab man qala li-imra'atihi anti 'ala haram, vol. 7, p. 574, no. 15056; Mussannaf Abd al-Razzaq, Bab al-Haram, vol. 6, p. 400, no. 11361; Mussannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, no. 49: 'Whoever said al-haram is an oath and not divorce', vol. 4, p. 99, no. 18183). (3) From Ibn Mas'ud: 'He used to say: His intention in haram is what he intended; if he did not intend divorce, then it is an oath.' (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, Bab man qala li-imra'atihi anti 'ala haram, vol. 7, p. 575, no. 15062; Mussannaf Abd al-Razzaq, no. 11366). From this athar it is known that if he has no intention in haram, an oath occurs. And if an oath occurs, then ila' also occurs. Footnote (continued from previous page): When he says 'she is haram on me,' he must free a slave, or fast two consecutive months, or feed sixty poor persons. (a) 'O Prophet, why do you forbid what Allah has made lawful to you...' (b) Ibn Abbas says: In the word haram, he must give kaffarah. (c) Ibn Mas'ud used to say: In the word haram, intention is considered, whatever he intends. And if he does not intend divorce, then an oath occurs.
Source pages p. 147

Commentary
This passage is a comprehensive treatment of the legal effect of the phrase 'anti 'ala haram' in Hanafi fiqh. The author, in his commentary, presents the rulings in a numbered sequence. The core principle: the word 'haram' is a kinaya (allusive word) that can mean different things depending on the intention of the speaker. There are five possible intentions outlined: (1) lying – no legal effect; (2) divorce – one irrevocable divorce occurs, unless three are intended, then three; (3) zihar – it becomes zihar, requiring kaffarah; (4) prohibition (tahrim) – it is an oath, making the husband a mu'li; (5) no intention – same as prohibition, an oath. The passage supports each ruling with athar (reports from the Companions and Successors), particularly from Sufyan al-Thawri, Ali, Zayd ibn Thabit, Ibn Abbas, and Ibn Mas'ud. The author also notes the view of al-Hasan al-Basri that intention is key. The footnote adds that for zihar, the kaffarah is freeing a slave, fasting two months, or feeding sixty poor. The passage emphasizes that the word 'haram' does not automatically effect divorce; rather, the speaker's intention (niyyah) determines the legal outcome. This is a fundamental principle in Hanafi law concerning allusive expressions in divorce and oaths.

Key Terms
الحرام (al-haram): In this context, an allusive word (kinaya) that can effect divorce, zihar, or an oath depending on the speaker's intention.
كناية (kinaya): An indirect expression whose legal effect is determined by the speaker's intention, as opposed to sarih (explicit) words.
بائن (ba'in): Irrevocable divorce where the husband cannot take back his wife without a new marriage contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, if a man says 'anti 'ala haram' with no specific intention, what is the ruling?
A) One irrevocable divorce
B) Zihar
C) An oath making him a mu'li
D) Nothing (it is a lie)

Key Takeaway
The phrase 'anti 'ala haram' is a kinaya whose legal outcome—divorce, zihar, oath, or nothing—is determined by the speaker's intention, not the literal meaning.

Talaq — Divorce
intermediate
6 min
Khul': Definition, Evidence, and Ruling
Definition, evidence, and ruling on khul' as bain divorce

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definition of khul', cite its Quranic and hadith proofs, and explain why the Hanafi school rules that khul' effects a single bain divorce.

Core Idea
Khul' is a wife-initiated divorce by paying compensation, and it immediately results in a single bain divorce.

Khul' is a special form of marital dissolution where the wife ransoms herself from the marriage by paying the husband. This lesson examines its definition, the primary textual evidence, and a key disagreement: does khul' itself terminate the marriage, or must the husband separately pronounce divorce? Understanding this ruling clarifies the legal status of the wife after khul' and the requirements for remarriage.

Guided Path
1
Define khul'
Identify the core elements: khul' is the termination of marriage by the wife giving compensation to the husband. The passage defines it as 'removing the marriage in exchange for wealth.'
Focus on the compensation aspect – it distinguishes khul' from regular talaq.
2
Examine the primary dalil
The verse (Al-Baqarah 2:229) permits the wife to ransom herself when the couple fears they cannot uphold Allah's limits. The hadith of Thabit's wife provides prophetic implementation.
The verse establishes permissibility; the hadith confirms that the Prophet (PBUH) accepted khul'.
3
Derive the Hanafi ruling on the effect of khul'
The passage cites an explicit hadith: 'The Prophet made khul' a single bain divorce.' Therefore, the Hanafi position is that khul' itself effects a bain divorce immediately.
No separate divorce pronouncement needed.
4
Identify the opposing view
Some scholars argue that khul' does not effect divorce based on another hadith where the Prophet ordered the husband to divorce after the compensation was taken, and an athar from Ibn Abbas.
These sources suggest khul' is merely a separation requiring a formal talaq.
5
Analyze the thamarah al-khilaf
If khul' is a bain divorce, the wife becomes a non-mahram and requires a new nikah to remarry the same husband. If not, the marriage may still be intact or only partially dissolved.
The practical difference affects the possibility of reunion without a new marriage contract.

باب الخلع

ضروری نوٹ ضلع کے معنی نکالنا ہیں، زوجیت کو مال کے بدلے میں نکال دینے کو ضلع کہتے ہیں ۔ ضلع میں بیوی کی جانب سے مال ہوتا ہے اور شوہر اس کے بدلے طلاق دیتا ہے اس کو ضلع کہتے ہیں۔ اس کا ثبوت اس آیت میں ہے۔ فان خفتم الا يقيما حدود الله فلا جناح عليهما فيما افتدت به (الف) ( آیت ۲۲۹ سورة البقرة (۲) (۲) اور اس حدیث میں بھی اس کا ثبوت ہے۔عن ابن عباس انه قال جائت امرأة ثابت بن قيس الى رسول الله اني لا اعتب على ثابت فى دين ولا خلق ولكني لا اطبقه فقال رسول الله فتر دین عیله حديقته ؟ قالت نعم (ب) ( بخاری شریف، باب الخلع و کیف الطلاق فیہ ص ۷۹۴ نمبر ۵۲۷۵) (ابوداؤد شریف، باب فی الخلع ص ۳۰۹ نمبر ۲۲۲۸) اس آیت اور حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ بیوی شوہر کے درمیان اختلاف ہو جائے تو ضلع کر سکتا ہے۔ [ ۲۰۰۵] (۱) اگر میاں بیوی میں ناچا کی ہو جائے اور دونوں خوف کرے کہ اللہ کی حدود کو قائم نہ کر سکے تو کوئی حرج نہیں ہے کہ عورت اپنی جان کے بدلے کچھ مال دے کر خلع کرے، پس جب انہوں نے یہ کر لیا تو خلع سے طلاق بائن واقع ہو جائے گی اور عورت کو مال لازم ہوگا ۔ میاں بیوی میں اختلاف ہو جائے اور اس بات کا خوف ہو کہ اللہ کی حدود کو قائم نہ کر سکے تو عورت کے لئے جائز ہے کہ شوہر کو کچھ مال دے کر طلاق لے لے اور اپنی جان چھڑالے ضلع کر کے شوہر مال لے تو ضلع کرتے ہی طلاق بائنہ واقع ہو جائے گی ۔ الگ سے طلاق دینے کی ضرورت نہیں ہے۔ ے ضلع جائز ہونے کی دلیل اوپر کی آیت اور حدیث ہے۔ اور ضلع ہی سے طلاق واقع ہو جائے گی اس کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن ابن عباسان النبي الا الله جعل الخلع تطليقة بائسة (ج) ( سفن المسيقى ، باب الخلع حل حوضخ او طلاق ج سابع ص ۳۱۶ مصنف ابن ابی شیبة ۱۰۴ ما قالوا فی الرجل اذا ضلع امرأته كم میكون من الطلاق؟ ج رابع ص ۸۵) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ ضلع خود ہی طلاق بائنہ ہے (۲) جب شوہر نے رقم لی تو اس کے بدلے عورت کی جان چھوٹی چاہئے اور یہ اسی شکل میں ہو سکتا ہے جبکہ ضلع طلاق بائنہ کے درجے میں ہو، اور نہ عورت کو رقم دینے سے فائدہ کیا ہوا ؟ بعض ائمہ کی رائے ہے کہ خلع سے طلاق واقع نہیں ہوگی بلکہ مال لینے کے بعد باضابطہ شوہر طلاق دے تب طلاق واقع ہوگی۔ ان کی دلیل اوپر کی حدیث کا یہ ٹکڑا ہے۔ عن عكرمة ان اخت عبد الله بن ابى بهذا وقال تردين حديقته ؟ قالت نعم فردتها وامرأة يطلقها (د) ( بخاری شریف، باب الخلع وكيف الطلاق فی ص ۷۹۴ نمبر ۵۲۷۴) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ بعد میں طلاق دے حاشیہ : (الف) اگر تم خوف کرو کہ میاں بیوی اللہ کی حدود کو قائم نہ کر سکے تو دونوں پر کوئی حرج کی بات نہیں ہے کہ عورت اس کا فدیہ دے (ب ) ثابت بن قیس کی بیوی حضور کے پاس آکر کہنے لگی یا رسول اللہ ! میں ثابت پر دین اور اخلاق کے بارے میں عیب نہیں لگاتی لیکن میں اس کے ساتھ رہنے کی طاقت نہیں رکھتی ۔ حضور نے پوچھا کیا اس کا باغ اس کو واپس دے سکتی ہے؟ کہنے لگی ہاں (ج) حضور نے ضلع کو طلاق بائنہ قرار دیا ( د ) آپ نے عبداللہ کی بہن سے فرمایا کیا تم (باقی اگلے صفحہ پر )

اس کا مطلب یہ ہوا کہ خلع طلاق نہیں ہے (۲) اثر میں ہے۔ سال ابراهیم بن سعد ابن عباس عن امرأة طلقها زوجها تطليقتين ثم اختلعت منه ايتزوجها ؟ قال ابن عباس ذكر الله عز وجل الطلاق اول الآية وآخرها والخلع بين ذلك فليس الخلع بطلاق ينكحها (الف) ( سنن للمبنی ، باب الخلع هل هو فسح او طلاق ؟ ج سابع مص ۵۱۷ نمبر ۱۳۸۶۳ مصنف ابن ابی شیبته ۱۰۶ من کان لایری الخلع طلاقاج رابع ص ۱۲۳ نمبر ۱۸۴۴۵) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ ضلع طلاق نہیں ہے۔
Book of Khul'. Chapter of Khul'. Necessary note: The meaning of khul' is to remove. To remove the marriage in exchange for wealth is called khul'. In khul', the wife gives wealth and the husband gives divorce in exchange. Its proof is in this verse: 'If you fear that they will not uphold the limits of Allah, then there is no sin upon them for what she ransoms herself with.' (Al-Baqarah 2:229) And also in this hadith: Ibn Abbas said: The wife of Thabit ibn Qays came to the Messenger of Allah and said: I do not blame Thabit for religion or character, but I cannot live with him. The Messenger of Allah said: 'Will you return to him his garden?' She said: Yes. (Bukhari, chapter of khul', no. 5275; Abu Dawud, chapter of khul', no. 2228). From this verse and hadith it is known that when discord occurs between husband and wife, they may perform khul'. [2005] (1) If there is discord between husband and wife and both fear they cannot uphold the limits of Allah, then there is no harm if the woman gives some wealth in exchange for her self and performs khul'. When they do that, a bain divorce occurs through khul' and the woman must pay the wealth. When husband and wife have discord and fear they cannot uphold Allah's limits, it is permissible for the woman to take divorce by giving some wealth to her husband and free herself. When the husband takes the wealth upon khul', with the khul' itself a bain divorce occurs. There is no need for a separate divorce. The proof that khul' is permissible is the above verse and hadith. And that divorce occurs through khul' itself is proved by this hadith: Ibn Abbas narrated that the Prophet made khul' a single bain divorce. (collections cited). This hadith shows that khul' itself is a bain divorce. (2) When the husband takes the wealth, in exchange the woman's self is freed, and this is only possible if khul' is in the category of bain divorce. Otherwise, what benefit would the payment be? Some imams are of the opinion that khul' does not effect divorce; rather, after taking the wealth, the husband must formally pronounce divorce. Their proof is this portion of the above hadith: Ikrimah narrated that the sister of Abdullah ibn Ubayy... and he said: 'Will you return his garden?' She said: Yes, and she returned it, and the Prophet ordered him to divorce her. (Bukhari no. 5274). This hadith indicates that the divorce is given afterward. Footnote: (a) If you fear that husband and wife cannot uphold Allah's limits, then there is no blame on them for the wife ransoming herself. (b) The wife of Thabit ibn Qays came to the Prophet... and said: I do not blame Thabit... but I cannot live with him. The Prophet asked: 'Can you return his garden?' She said: Yes. (c) The Prophet declared khul' a bain divorce. (d) The Prophet said to the sister of Abdullah... 'Will you...' (continued on next page). This means that khul' is not a divorce. (2) There is an athar: Ibrahim ibn Sa'd asked Ibn Abbas about a woman whose husband had divorced her twice, then she performed khul' from him: can he marry her? Ibn Abbas said: Allah mentioned divorce at the beginning and end of the verse, and khul' is between that, so khul' is not divorce; he may marry her. (Sunan al-Mubni? and Ibn Abi Shayba). This athar shows that khul' is not a divorce.
Source pages p. 149

Commentary
This passage is a ruling-with-proof that defines khul', provides its Quranic and prophetic evidence, states the Hanafi ruling that khul' effects a single bain divorce, and then presents an intra-madhhab or inter-madhhab dispute about whether khul' itself is a divorce or merely a separation requiring a separate divorce. The passage begins with a definition: khul' is the dissolution of marriage by the wife paying compensation. The primary evidence is the Quranic verse (2:229) which permits the wife to ransom herself when the couple fears they cannot uphold Allah's limits. A hadith from Thabit ibn Qays's wife corroborates this. The text then presents the core ruling: when khul' is performed with compensation, a bain divorce occurs immediately. A separate hadith is cited where the Prophet explicitly made khul' a single bain divorce. The commentary emphasizes that no separate divorce is needed. Then the passage notes that some scholars disagree: they hold that khul' does not effect a divorce; rather, the husband must formally divorce after receiving the compensation. They cite a version of the hadith where the Prophet ordered the husband to divorce. Additionally, an athar from Ibn Abbas is quoted, where he says that khul' is not divorce because the verse mentions divorce separately before and after mentioning khul'. This presents a clear ikhtilaf. The Hanafi position, based on the explicit hadith that the Prophet declared khul' a bain divorce, is that khul' itself is a divorce. The practical consequence is that after khul', the couple cannot remarry without a new nikah.

Key Terms
خلع (khul'): A divorce initiated by the wife in exchange for compensation (usually money or property) paid to the husband.
طلاق بائن (talaq bain): An irrevocable divorce that ends the marriage immediately; the couple cannot remarry without a new marriage contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the legal effect of khul' on the marriage?
A) It is a revocable divorce (raj'i).
B) It is a single bain divorce (talaq bain).
C) It is an annulment (faskh) without divorce.
D) It requires a separate divorce pronouncement by the husband.

Key Takeaway
Khul' is a valid form of divorce in the Hanafi school that immediately results in a single bain divorce upon the wife's payment of compensation and the husband's acceptance.

Ruling When Nushuz Is from the Husband
States the ruling when the husband is the disobedient party: it is makruh for him to take compensation in khul'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on taking compensation in khul' when the husband is the nushuz party and identify the proof from hadith.

Core Idea
It is makruh for a husband to take khul' compensation when his own nushuz forces the wife to seek divorce.

Khul' allows a wife to separate from her husband by paying compensation. But what if the husband's own misconduct forces her to do so? In this passage, Al-Hidayah addresses that scenario: taking compensation in such a case is makruh (disliked) and close to haram. The key principle is that wealth must be given willingly, and a husband at fault cannot profit from his wrongdoing.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the husband taking compensation (damages) from the wife in a khul' divorce. The ruling is that it is makruh (disliked) for him to take anything when his own nushuz (disobedience) is the cause.
Makruh here is makruh tahrimi, near-haram, due to the hadith prohibition.
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
The text cites two proofs: a hadith from the Prophet (peace be upon him) at Mina forbidding taking a brother's wealth without willing consent, and an athar from Zuhri stating that if the husband's nushuz is proven, the compensation should be returned to the wife.
The hadith is from Dar Qutni, the athar from Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah (how the proof applies)
The hadith explicitly prohibits taking wealth without the owner's free consent. In this case, the wife is not giving willingly; she is compelled by the husband's misconduct. Therefore, the husband's taking is included in the prohibition, making it makruh (close to haram).
The athar provides the practical consequence: if proven, the money is returned.
4
Note the ikhtilaf (disagreement)
Some schools may permit the husband to take compensation regardless of fault. The Hanafi school specifies that fault matters, and only when the wife is the nushuz party is compensation fully permissible.
This ruling is specific to Hanafi fiqh; other madhahib may differ.
5
Apply the ruling
In practice, if a husband's nushuz is established (e.g., abuse, neglect), he should not ask for or accept any compensation in khul'. If he does, and the fault is proven, a court may order the return of the compensation to the wife.
The ruling protects the wife from further injustice and upholds the principle of willing consent.

Source Text

منه بمال يخلعها به فاذا فعل ذلك وقع بالخلع تطليقة بائنة ولزمها المال ۲۰۰۶ (۲) وان كان النشوز من قبله كره له ان يأخذ منها عوضا. اگر نافرمانی مرد کی جانب سے ہو تو اس کے لئے مکر وہ ہے کہ عورت سے عوض لے۔ شرارت مرد کی ہے جس کی وجہ سے عورت ضلع کرنے پر مجبور ہے تو مرد کو عوض لینا مکروہ ہے۔ جہ اس لئے کہ مرد کی شرارت بھی ہے اور مجبور کر کے عوض بھی لے رہا ہے تو یہ خوشی سے نہیں ہوا۔ اور بغیر خوشی کے مال لینا اچھا نہیں ہے۔ عـن عمرو بن يثربي قال شهدت رسول الله الله في حجة الوداع بمنى فسمعته يقول لا يحل لامرء من مال اخيه شيء الا ماطابت به نفسه (ب) (دار قطنی ، کتاب البیوع ج ثالث ص ۲۲ نمبر ۲۸۶۰) اثر میں ہے۔ عن الزهري قال اذا افتدت امرأة من زوجها واخرجت البينة ان النشوز كان من قبله وانه كان يضرها ويضارها رد اليها مالها (ج) (مصنف عبد الرزاق، باب بيضار هاتی تخلع مندج سادس ص ۵۰۱ نمبر ۱۱۸۳۵) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ اگر شوہر کی شرارت ہو تو تم بیوی کو واپس کی جائے۔
From him with wealth by which he performs khul' with her; when he does that, a bain divorce occurs through khul' and the wealth becomes obligatory upon her. [2006] (2) And if the nushuz (disobedience) is from his side, it is disliked (makruh) for him to take compensation from her. If the disobedience is from the husband's side, then it is makruh for him to take compensation from the wife. The mischief is from the man, due to which the woman is forced to perform khul', so it is makruh for the man to take compensation. This is because the man's mischief exists and he is taking compensation under compulsion; it is not given willingly. Taking wealth without willingness is not good. From Amr ibn Yathribi: I witnessed the Messenger of Allah at Mina during the Farewell Pilgrimage and heard him say: 'It is not permissible for a man to take anything from his brother's wealth except what he gives willingly.' (Dar Qutni, Book of Sales, vol. 3, p. 22, no. 2860). There is an athar: From Zuhri: He said, 'If a woman performs khul' from her husband and brings evidence that the nushuz was from him and that he was harming her and harassing her, then her wealth is returned to her.' (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, chapter on...). This athar shows that if the husband's mischief is proven, the wife's compensation is returned to her.
Source pages p. 150

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling with proof regarding the situation where the husband is the disobedient party (nushuz). The matn states that if nushuz is from the husband's side, it is makruh (disliked) for him to take any compensation from the wife in khul'. The commentary explains the reasoning: since the husband's own misconduct is forcing the wife to seek khul', taking her money would be unjust—she is not giving it willingly. The principle is that taking someone's wealth without their free consent is impermissible. The hadith from Amr ibn Yathribi is cited as a proof: the Prophet forbade taking a brother's wealth except with his willing consent. Additionally, an athar from Zuhri indicates that if it is proven that the husband was at fault, the wife's compensation should be returned to her. Thus, the ruling discourages the husband from profiting from his own wrongdoing. This is specific to the Hanafi school's detailed rulings on khul'.

Key Terms
نشوز (nushuz): Disobedience or discord, i.e., when one spouse fails to fulfill marital duties or behaves hostilely.
مكروه (makruh): Disliked; an act that is not sinful but is discouraged. In this context, it is close to haram due to the hadith.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) When you ask permission.
B) When he gives it willingly.
C) When you deserve it.
D) When it is a loan.

Key Takeaway
When the husband's nushuz forces the wife to seek khul', it is makruh (near-haram) for him to take any compensation, as it contradicts the principle of willing consent.

Ruling When Nushuz Is from the Wife
States the ruling when wife is disobedient

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the husband taking compensation when the wife's nushuz leads to khul', and explain why taking more than the equivalent is makruh.

Core Idea
When the wife is disobedient, the husband should not take more than he gave her in khul'.

This passage addresses a common scenario in marital disputes: if the wife is the cause of discord (nushuz) and khul' occurs, can the husband take more compensation than the mahr or gifts he gave? The Hanafi ruling restricts him to the equivalent, and taking more is disliked. The proof comes from the prophetic hadith of Thabit's wife.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
What is being ruled upon? The act is the husband taking compensation in khul' when nushuz is from the wife. The ruling is that it is makruh (disliked) to take more than the equivalent of what he gave her.
The text explicitly states 'it is makruh for the husband to take more.'
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the hadith of Thabit ibn Qays's wife, where the Prophet (peace be upon him) permitted the husband to take the garden (the dower) but did not allow more. This is found in Bukhari and other collections.
Though not directly quoted in the truncated text, the context references it.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's permission to take the garden alone indicates that taking more would be impermissible or disliked. The command 'take what you gave' implies no excess. Hence, taking more is contrary to the prophetic guidance.
This establishes the legal link between the hadith and the ruling.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) allow the husband and wife to agree on any compensation, irrespective of fault, as long as both consent. The Hanafi school restricts it when the wife is the cause of discord.
The difference arises from interpretation of the hadith and the verse on khul'.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi position is based on the principle of justice: the husband should not profit from the wife's disobedience. The hadith of Thabit's wife is understood as setting a limit.
This is the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school.

This athar shows that khul' is not a divorce.

Key Terms
نشوز (nushuz): Disobedience of the wife towards her husband without legitimate reason.
خلع (khul'): Divorce initiated by the wife in return for compensation paid to the husband.

Key Takeaway
When nushuz is from the wife, the husband may only take the equivalent of his gift in khul'; taking more is makruh.

Khul' as Ba'in Talaq: Offer and Acceptance Constitute Divorce
Ruling on khul' with proof from hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that khul' is itself a ba'in talaq and explain the proof from the hadith of Ibn Abbas.

Core Idea
Khul' is itself a talaq; mutual offer and acceptance create an irrevocable ba'in divorce with binding consideration.

This passage establishes a foundational ruling in Hanafi family law: when a husband says 'I divorce you for such-and-such wealth' and the wife accepts, the divorce is effective immediately and is irrevocable (ba'in). No separate pronouncement of talaq is needed. The passage then cites a hadith to prove that khul' is a single ba'in talaq, distinguishing the Hanafi position from other schools that view khul' as an annulment.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is khul' (divorce for consideration). The ruling: talaq occurs upon acceptance, consideration becomes wajib, and the talaq is ba'in.
Note that khul' itself is a talaq, not a separate procedure.
2
Locate the dalil
The text cites a hadith from Ibn Abbas that the Prophet (peace be upon him) declared khul' to be a single ba'in talaq.
The hadith is ahad, so it provides zanni thubut but qati dalala.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The phrase 'تطليقة بائنة' directly states the ruling. The word 'بائنة' indicates irrevocability.
Hanafi usul: a clear explicit text (nass) yields certainty in meaning.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some schools (e.g., Shafi'i) view khul' as faskh (annulment), not talaq, affecting the count of remaining talaqs.
The practical consequence: after khul', the husband has the remaining number of talaqs if it is ba'in sughra.
5
Evaluate the proof strength
The Hanafi school relies on this hadith and the principle that the offer and acceptance constitute a complete legal act.
No need for separate talaq; the khul' contract itself effects the divorce.

And if he divorces her for a consideration and she accepts, the talaq occurs and the consideration becomes binding upon her, and the talaq is ba'in. And if he gave talaq for wealth and the woman accepted, then talaq will occur and the wealth will be binding on her, and the talaq will be ba'in. Source pages p. 151

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from the Hanafi madhhab on khul'. It states that when a husband says to his wife 'I divorce you for such-and-such wealth' and she accepts, the talaq occurs immediately upon her acceptance, and she becomes liable for the agreed consideration. No separate pronouncement of talaq is needed because khul' itself is a form of talaq. The talaq here is ba'in (irrevocable), meaning the husband cannot take her back without a new marriage contract. The text then cites a hadith from Ibn Abbas that the Prophet (peace be upon him) declared khul' to be a single ba'in talaq, establishing the proof. The Urdu commentary explains that the husband's proposal is an offer (ijab) and the wife's acceptance (qabul) completes the contract. The consideration is binding because it was a condition of the talaq. The hadith is the primary dalil for the classification of khul' as ba'in.

Key Terms
خلع (khul'): Divorce initiated by the wife in exchange for compensation paid to the husband, which constitutes a ba'in talaq.
طلاق بائن (talaq ba'in): An irrevocable divorce where the husband cannot take back his wife without a new marriage contract and a new mahr.
عوض ('iwad): The consideration paid by the wife to the husband in exchange for khul'.

Khul' with Invalid Consideration: Ba'in Separation
Ruling with proof on khul' with invalid consideration.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on khul' with invalid consideration and explain why the separation is ba'in.

Core Idea
Khul' with invalid consideration is valid as ba'in talaq, but the husband receives nothing.

Khul' requires a valid consideration (iwad) from the wife. But what if she offers something that Islamic law does not recognize as property, like wine or a pig? Does the khul' still take effect? This lesson clarifies the Hanafi position: the talaq is valid and irrevocable, even though the husband gets nothing.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what act is being ruled upon and its hukm level. Here, the act is khul' with invalid consideration. The ruling: khul' is sahih (valid), the husband receives no compensation, and the separation is ba'in (irrevocable).
The hukm level is 'sahih' for the khul' itself, not a separate category.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the proof cited. The author refers to a hadith: 'The Prophet (صلى الله عليه وسلم) made khul' a single ba'in talaq.' This hadith is the primary textual evidence.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) but its meaning is considered qat'i (clear) in this context.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Explain how the hadith proves the ruling. The hadith establishes that khul' itself results in ba'in talaq. This applies regardless of the validity of the consideration. Since the khul' is valid, the talaq is ba'in, and no compensation is due because the consideration is not legally recognized.
The invalidity of the consideration does not affect the talaq; it only affects the compensation.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Identify any scholarly disagreement. The Shafi'i school may consider such a khul' as faskh (annulment) without compensation, but the Hanafi school maintains it is a valid ba'in talaq.
This difference affects whether the husband can remarry the wife without a new mahr.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
Confirm the mufta bihi position: the husband gets nothing and the separation is ba'in. This is based on the hadith and the Hanafi principle that kinayah (indirect expression) results in ba'in talaq.
The word 'khul' is kinayah, which by default leads to ba'in talaq per Hanafi usul.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

And if the consideration in khul' becomes invalid, such as if he makes khul' with a Muslim woman for wine or a pig, then nothing is due to the husband and the separation is ba'in. And if the consideration becomes invalid in khul', e.g., a Muslim woman makes khul' for wine or pig, then the husband gets nothing and the separation is ba'in. The woman promised to give something that is not property for a Muslim, e.g., wine or pig, so the consideration became invalid. Commentary
This passage rules on a scenario where the consideration (iwad) in khul' is something that is not legally considered property for a Muslim, such as wine or a pig. According to the Hanafi madhhab, the khul' is still valid as a divorce, but since the consideration is invalid (non-existent in Islamic law), the husband is not entitled to anything. The separation is ba'in (irrevocable) because the word khul' is kinayah (indirect) and, per the hadith, results in a ba'in talaq. The Urdu commentary explains that the wife cannot give wine or pig as they are not lawful property, nor can she give their value. Therefore, the husband receives nothing. However, the talaq itself occurs and is ba'in. The footnote reinforces that the Prophet established khul' as ba'in talaq.

Invalid Consideration in Explicit Talaq (Talaq Sarih) Results in Raj'i Talaq
Distinction between khul' and talaq when consideration is invalid

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when consideration in a talaq (explicit word 'talaq') is invalid, and distinguish the outcome from khul'.

Core Idea
When the word 'talaq' is explicit, invalid consideration does not make the divorce ba'in; it remains raj'i.

In previous lessons, we learned that in khul', invalid consideration leads to ba'in talaq. However, when the husband uses the explicit word 'talaq', the ruling differs. This lesson clarifies that the word 'talaq' itself establishes a revocable divorce; an invalid condition attached to it is simply void, leaving the talaq as raj'i.

Guided Path
1
Identify the trigger
The husband says 'I divorce you' (or equivalent explicit word) with a condition involving invalid consideration (e.g., a pig as payment).
The word used must be sarih (explicit) like 'talaq', not kinayah.
2
Determine the type of word
Check whether the pronouncement is sarih (explicit) or kinayah (allusive). Here it is sarih.
Sarih talaq does not require intention for effect; it operates automatically.
3
Apply the principle of sarih talaq
Sarih talaq normally results in raj'i talaq unless conditions or wording make it ba'in (e.g., triple talaq, or mention of ba'in).
Invalid consideration does not transform the nature of the talaq.
4
Evaluate the condition
The condition of invalid consideration (like wine or pig) is void (batil) in Islamic law. Therefore, it is as if no condition was stipulated.
A void condition does not affect the validity of the talaq itself.
5
Conclude the ruling
Since the condition is void and the word used is sarih talaq, the divorce is valid and raj'i. The husband may revoke it during the iddah period.
No consideration is due to the wife; the talaq is simply revocable.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وان بطل العوض في الطلاق كان رجعيا اور اگر عوض باطل ہو طلاق میں تو رجعی ہوگی۔  (۶) اور اگر عوض باطل ہو طلاق میں تو رجعی ہوگی۔ حاشیہ: (الف) حضور نے ضلع کو طلاق بائنہ قرار دیا۔
And if the consideration becomes invalid in talaq, it is raj'i. And if consideration becomes invalid in talaq, it will be raj'i. Footnote: (a) The Prophet declared khul' to be ba'in talaq.
Source pages p. 151

Commentary
This ruling distinguishes between khul' and regular talaq. In previous rulings, when the consideration in khul' was invalid, the separation was ba'in. Here, if the husband uses the explicit word 'talaq' (not 'khul') and the consideration (such as wine or pig) is invalid, the talaq is raj'i (revocable). The reason is that the word 'talaq' is sarih (explicit), which normally results in a revocable talaq unless it is expressly made ba'in by conditions. Since the consideration is invalid, it is as if no consideration was agreed, and the talaq remains raj'i. The footnote reasserts that khul' is ba'in per the hadith.

Key Terms
طلاق رجعي (talaq raj'i): A revocable divorce where the husband can take his wife back within the iddah without a new marriage contract.
عوض باطل (iwad batil): Invalid consideration, such as wine, pig, or anything not recognized as proper property in Islamic law.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Talaq is ba'in
C) Talaq is raj'i

Key Takeaway
When 'talaq' is explicit, invalid consideration does not nullify or change the divorce to ba'in; the talaq remains raj'i.

Equating Khul' Consideration with Mahr
Rule equating valid mahr items with valid khul' consideration

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi qiyas that equates valid mahr items with valid khul' consideration to determine the permissibility of various items as khul' badal.

Core Idea
Any item valid as mahr is valid as khul' consideration because both are compensation for the marital relation.

This passage uses qiyas (analogical reasoning) to extend the permissibility of mahr items to khul' consideration. The key insight is that both mahr and khul' badal are forms of compensation (badal) for the marital relationship (bud'). By understanding this reasoning, you can identify which items are acceptable in khul' without being limited to cash.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling and its Scope
The passage rules that whatever is permissible as mahr in marriage is permissible as badal (consideration) in khul'. This applies to all items that can serve as mahr.
The ruling is about permissibility, not obligation.
2
Recognize the Qiyas Structure
The qiyas has asl (nikah with mahr), far' (khul'), and illa (both are badal al-bud' – compensation for the right of intimacy). The hukm of the asl (validity of certain items as mahr) is transferred to the far'.
The illa is jaliyyah (clear) because both transactions involve exchange for marital rights.
3
Verify the Illa
The text states: 'Mahr is compensation for the right of intimacy, and in khul' too there is a kind of compensation for that right.' This confirms the illa is consistent and valid.
4
Apply the Ruling to Examples
Test hypothetical items: gold, silver, a car, a house – if they can be mahr, they can be khul' badal. The key condition is that the item must be mal mutaqawwim (valuable property) and known (ma'lum).
Items like alcohol or pork cannot be mahr, so they also cannot be khul' badal.
5
Note Exceptions and Conditions
The item must be permissible property. If it is not mal mutaqawwim (e.g., a haram item), it cannot be valid. Also, the amount or value does not need to be equal to the mahr; only the permissibility category matters.
This ruling facilitates khul' by not restricting to cash only.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وما جازان يكون مهرا في النكاح جاز ان يكون بدلا في الخلع [۲۰۱۱] (۷) جو چیز جائز ہے کہ نکاح میں مہر بنے جائز ہے کہ وہ ضلع میں بدل ہے۔ جو چیز نکاح میں مہر بن سکتی ہو وہ ضلع میں بدل بن سکتی ہے۔ مبر بضع کا بدلا ہے۔ اور ضلع میں بھی ایک قسم کا بضع کا بدلا ہے اس لئے جو چیز نکاح میں مہر بن سکتی ہے وہ ضلع میں بدل بن سکتی ہے۔
And whatever is permissible to be mahr in marriage is permissible to be a substitute (badal) in khul'. (7) Whatever thing is permissible to be mahr in marriage, it is permissible that it be a substitute in khul'. Whatever can be mahr in nikah can be a substitute in khul'. Mahr is compensation for the right of intimacy (buda'), and in khul' too there is a kind of compensation for that right, so whatever can be mahr in nikah can be a substitute in khul'.
Source pages p. 152

Commentary
This passage establishes a qiyas (analogical reasoning) between mahr in nikah and badal (consideration) in khul'. The basis is that both are compensations for the marital relationship (badal al-bud'): mahr is for the right of intimacy in marriage, and khul' is for the dissolution of that right. Therefore, any item that is valid as mahr (i.e., property of value, permissible, known) is also valid as consideration in khul'. This includes cash, goods, services, etc., as long as they are property (mal mutaqawwim).

Key Terms
بدل (badal): Substitute or consideration in khul', analogous to mahr.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

C) No, because khul' requires tangible property
D) Yes, but only if husband has no other income

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school facilitates khul' by allowing any property that can be mahr to be given as consideration.

Unspecified 'What is in Hand' Yields No Consideration if Empty
Ruling on khul' for unspecified 'what is in my hand' when hand is empty

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a khul' where the wife offers 'what is in my hand' without specifying wealth and her hand is empty, and explain why no consideration is due.

Core Idea
If the wife offers khul' for 'what is in my hand' without mentioning 'wealth', and her hand is empty, nothing is owed.

In Hanafi law, the validity of khul' depends on the specification and existence of the consideration. When a wife says 'khul' me for what is in my hand,' she does not explicitly promise wealth. If her hand is empty, the condition is unfulfilled, and the husband receives no compensation. This lesson examines the rationale behind this ruling and its practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the wife's offer
The wife says 'khul' me for what is in my hand' – note that she does not say 'wealth' or 'mal'. The term 'what is in my hand' is ambiguous.
2
Determine if the consideration is specified as wealth
The Hanafi position requires that the consideration be explicitly identified as 'mal' (wealth) to be binding. Here, it is not specified.
If she had said 'for the wealth in my hand', the ruling would differ.
3
Evaluate the existence of the consideration
Even if the phrase were considered a promise, the fact that her hand is empty means the consideration does not exist.
Existence is a condition for obligation.
4
Apply the Hanafi rule
Since the condition is ambiguous and the subject matter nonexistent, no compensation is due. The khul' itself is valid and results in a ba'in divorce.
5
Conclude the ruling
The husband gets nothing; the separation stands without financial burden on the wife.
This preserves the wife's financial independence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فان قالت خالعنى على ما فى يدى فخالعها ولم يكن في يدها شيء فلا شيء له عليها [ ۲۰۱۲] (۸) اگر عورت نے کہا مجھ سے ضلع کریں اس کے بدلے جو میرے ہاتھ میں ہے، پس اس سے خلع کیا اور اس کے ہاتھ میں کچھ نہیں تھا تو شوہر کے لئے عورت پر کچھ لازم نہیں ہوگا وجہ عورت نے یہ نہیں کہا کہ جو مال میرے ہاتھ میں ہے اس کے بدلے ضلع کریں۔ چونکہ مال کا نام نہیں لیا اور ہاتھ میں کچھ نہیں تھا تو عورت پر کوئی مال لازم نہیں ہوگا۔
For if she says 'Khul' me for what is in my hand' and he makes khul' with her, but there was nothing in her hand, then nothing is due from her. (8) If the woman said 'Khul' me in exchange for what is in my hand', then he made khul' and there was nothing in her hand, then nothing is binding upon the woman for the husband. The reason is that the woman did not say 'for the wealth that is in my hand'. Since she did not name wealth and there was nothing in her hand, no wealth is binding upon her.
Source pages p. 152

Commentary
This is a ruling on the specificity of consideration in khul'. The wife offers a consideration described as 'what is in my hand' without mentioning 'wealth'. According to Hanafi fiqh, this is ambiguous. Since she did not specify that there is wealth (mal), and her hand is empty, nothing is due to the husband. The khul' is still valid, and the separation is ba'in (as established earlier), but the husband gets no financial compensation because the condition was not fulfilled. The principle is that a condition of something uncertain in existence is void, and the khul' stands without consideration.

Key Terms
ما في يدها (ma fi yadiha): What is in her hand – ambiguous phrase that does not necessarily imply wealth.
خلع (khul'): Divorce initiated by the wife in exchange for compensation.
مال (mal): Wealth or property; specific mention of mal is required for the consideration to be binding in khul' if the phrase is ambiguous.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The khul' is invalid and she must give her mahr.
B) The khul' is valid and she must give the equivalent of three dirhams.
C) The khul' is valid and nothing is due from her.
D) The khul' is suspended until she acquires something in her hand.

Key Takeaway
An ambiguous consideration in khul' without specification of wealth and without actual existence does not obligate the wife to pay anything.

Unspecified Wealth in Hand Requires Returning Mahr if Empty
Ruling when wife says khul' for wealth in hand but hand is empty

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi default rule that when a khul' consideration is unspecified and unrealized, the wife must return her mahr.

Core Idea
If a wife offers 'wealth in her hand' for khul' but has nothing, she must return her mahr.

This lesson examines a specific scenario in khul' where the wife proposes a consideration that turns out to be non-existent. How does the Hanafi school resolve the ambiguity? The ruling hinges on a default reference to the previously established dower (mahr).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the offered consideration
The act is khul' (divorce initiated by wife with compensation). The consideration is 'what is in my hand of wealth' – unspecified and later found to be empty.
2
Determine the legal consequence when the consideration is absent
Since she promised wealth but had none, the husband is entitled to compensation. The default is not the market value but a known benchmark.
3
Apply the Hanafi principle of defaulting to the mahr
Because no specific amount was named, the previously established wealth (the mahr) between the spouses is used. The wife must return the mahr she received at marriage.
This principle derives from the maxim: when something is unspecified, the prior covenanted (ma'hood) value is binding.

Source Text

وان قالت خالعنى على ما فى يدى من مال فخالعها ولم يكن في يدها شيء ردت عليها مهرها ١٠٠ وان قالت خالعنى على ما في يدى من دراهم عورت نے خلع کا لفظ استعمال نہیں کیا بلکہ طلاق کا لفظ استعمال کیا کہ طلاق کے بدلے مال ہو۔ [ ۲۰۱۳] (۹) اور اگر کہا مجھ سے ضلع کریں اس کے بدلے جو میرے ہاتھ میں ہے مال میں سے، پس اس سے ضلع کیا اور عورت کے ہاتھ میں کچھ نہیں تھا تو عورت اپنا مہر واپس دے گی۔ اس صورت میں عورت نے کہا ہے جو مال میرے ہاتھ میں ہے اس کے بدلے خلع کریں اور عورت کے ہاتھ میں کچھ نہیں تھا تو عورت کو میں نے کہا جو کے بدلے اور کے ہاتھ میں کچھ تا مہر واپس کرنا ہوگا۔ یہاں کوئی مال متعین نہیں ہے۔ البتہ دونوں کے درمیان ایک مال پہلے متعین ہو چکا ہے یعنی مہر اس لئے مجبورا مہر کی طرف پھیرا جائے گا اور وہی لازم کیا جائے گا۔ کیونکہ شوہر سے مال کا وعدہ کیا ہے اس لئے وہ کوئی مال لئے بغیر طلاق دینے پر راضی نہیں ہو گا۔ اصول یہ مسئلہ اس اصول پر ہے کہ کوئی چیز متعین نہ ہو تو جو پہلے سے معہود و متعین ہو وہی لازم کر دیا جائے گا۔
And if she says 'Khul' me for what is in my hand of wealth' and he makes khul' with her, but there was nothing in her hand, she must return her mahr to him. (9) And if she said 'Make khul' with me in exchange for what is in my hand from wealth', and he did khul', and there was nothing in her hand, then the woman must return her mahr. In this case, the woman said 'khul' for the wealth in my hand', and there was nothing in her hand, so she must return the mahr. Here there is no specific wealth; however, there is a prior known wealth between them, i.e., the mahr. Therefore, it is turned back to the mahr, and that is made binding. The principle is that when something is not specified, the previously covenanted (ma'hood) and specified wealth is made binding.
Source pages p. 152

Commentary
This ruling addresses a scenario where the wife specifies 'wealth' (mal) in her hand as the consideration for khul', but upon execution, her hand is empty. Since she mentioned 'wealth', the husband expected some compensation. However, no specific amount or item was named. According to Hanafi fiqh, when a consideration is promised but not specified, and the actual item does not exist, the default is to refer to the mahr (dower) that the husband gave her at marriage. This is because the mahr is a known and established wealth between them. The principle applied is: when no specific consideration is named but some compensation is implied, the previously established transaction (the mahr) is taken as the standard. Thus, she must return her mahr to the husband.

Key Terms
مهر (mahr): The dower given by husband to wife at marriage; here it becomes the default consideration.

Key Takeaway
When a khul' consideration is unspecified and unrealized, the Hanafi school defaults to the mahr as the agreed-upon benchmark.

Khul' with Unspecified Dirhams: The Minimum Plural Rule
Ruling when wife promises unspecified dirhams in khul' but has none.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when a wife promises unspecified dirhams in khul' but her hand is empty and explain why three dirhams are wajib.

Core Idea
When a wife promises 'dirhams' as khul' consideration but has none, the minimum plural (three) becomes wajib.

This lesson examines a specific scenario in khul' where the wife offers 'the dirhams in my hand' as consideration, but her hand is empty. The Hanafi school applies the linguistic principle that a plural form implies at least three, thus obligating three dirhams. Understanding this rule clarifies how vague promises are resolved in Islamic family law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the wife's khul' promise of 'dirhams in her hand' as consideration. The ruling: if her hand is empty, she must pay three dirhams.
This is a default ruling when the promised amount is unspecified.
2
Understand the linguistic principle
In Arabic, a plural (جمع) indicates at least three. 'Dirhams' (دراهم) is a plural, so its minimum is three.
This principle is used in Hanafi fiqh to avoid contractual uncertainty.
3
Apply the principle to the case
Since the wife said 'dirhams' (plural) and her hand is empty, the law infers the minimum of that plural: three dirhams.
If she had some dirhams, those would be due; emptiness triggers the default.
4
State the consequence
She owes three dirhams to the husband. This makes the khul' valid and enforceable.
The ruling applies whether she says 'dirhams' with or without the definite article.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وان قالت خالعنى على ما في يدى من دراهم عورت نے خلع کا لفظ استعمال نہیں کیا بلکہ طلاق کا لفظ استعمال کیا کہ طلاق کے بدلے مال ہو۔ پھر سور اور شراب ہونے کی وجہ سے عوض باطل ہو گیا تو طلاق رجعی واقع ہوگی۔ يہاں طلاق صریح استعمال کیا ہے اس لئے اگر اس کے بدلے مال ہوتا تو طلاق بائنہ واقع ہوتی۔ لیکن عوض باطل ہو گیا اس لئے صرف طلاق صریح باقی رہی۔ اس لئے اس سے طلاق رجعی واقع ہوگی۔ [ ۲۰۱۴] (۱۰) اور اگر کہا مجھ سے ضلع کرو اس کے بدلے جو میرے ہاتھ میں ہے عام یا خاص درہموں میں سے، پس اگر ایسا کر لیا اور نہیں تھا اس کے ہاتھ میں کچھ تو عورت پر تین درہم لازم ہیں۔ در اہم جمع کا صیغہ ہے جس کا اطلاق کم سے کم تین پر ہوتا ہے۔ اس لئے الف لام کے بغیر در اھم نکرہ استعمال کرے یا الف لام کے ساتھ
And if she says 'Khul' me for what is in my hand of dirhams'... The woman did not use the word khul' but used the word talaq, saying that for talaq there is wealth. Then due to wine and pig the consideration becomes invalid, so talaq is raj'i. Here explicit talaq was used, so if there was wealth in exchange, it would be ba'in talaq. But when the consideration became invalid, only explicit talaq remained, so talaq raj'i occurs. (10) And if she said 'Make khul' with me in exchange for what is in my hand, from general or specific dirhams', and he did so, but there was nothing in her hand, then three dirhams are due from her. Dirhams is a plural form which applies to a minimum of three. So whether she uses 'dirham' without alif lam as indefinite or with alif lam...

Commentary
This last passage initially revisits the distinction between khul' and explicit talaq with invalid consideration, repeating earlier lesson (6). Then it presents new ruling (10): If the wife specifies 'dirhams' (plural) in her hand as the consideration for khul', but her hand is empty, the minimum three dirhams become due. The reason is that the word 'dirhams' (دراهم) is a plural, and the minimum plural in Arabic is three. Thus, in default, she must pay three dirhams. The commentary notes that whether she says 'dirhams' without definite article or with it, the same applies. This is an application of the principle that when a vague quantity of a specific currency is promised, the minimum of the plural is taken.

Key Terms
دراهم (darahim): Plural of dirham; minimum three is due when unspecified.

When a wife promises unspecified dirhams in khul' but has none, the minimum of three dirhams becomes wajib due to the linguistic rule that a plural indicates at least three.

Proportional Compensation in Khul' When Fewer Divorces Are Given
Ruling with supporting athar from al-Thawri and al-Zuhri

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling and explain the proportional division of khul' compensation when fewer divorces are given than requested.

Core Idea
Compensation for khul' is divided proportionally among the divorces; fewer divorces mean less payment.

When a wife offers a lump sum for multiple divorces but receives fewer, the compensation must be adjusted proportionally. This lesson examines the Hanafi rule based on the particle 'ba' indicating exchange, supported by an athar from al-Thawri and al-Zuhri.

Guided Path
1
Identify the request and the actual number of divorces
The wife requested three divorces for a fixed sum (1000 dirhams). The husband gave only one divorce. Note the difference between what was requested and what was given.
The request is for multiple divorces, but the husband's action is limited to one.
2
Apply the principle of badaliyyah (exchange)
The particle 'ba' indicates that the sum is compensation for the divorces. Therefore, the total compensation is divided equally among the requested divorces.
Each requested divorce corresponds to one-third of the sum.
3
Calculate the owed amount
Since only one divorce was given, the wife owes one-third of the total sum (333.33 dirhams). The athar confirms this calculation.
The divorce becomes ba'in because it is a khul' transaction.
4
Recognize the authority of the athar
The athar from al-Thawri and al-Zuhri directly supports this ruling. It is a mursal hadith, accepted in Hanafi fiqh as a valid proof for this type of case.
The athar explicitly states: 'He gets one-third of the thousand, and she is irrevocably divorced once.'

معرفہ استعمال کرے دونوں صورتوں میں تین درہم لازم ہوں گے۔
