A) Three times
B) Four times
C) Five times
D) Two times

Key Takeaway
Li'an must begin with the husband, who swears four times affirming his truthfulness, then a fifth time invoking the curse; the wife then swears four times denying and a fifth invoking wrath.

Talaq — Divorce
intermediate
12 min
The Li'an Procedure and the Nature of Separation
Describes li'an procedure and its legal consequence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the steps of the li'an procedure and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the resulting separation, identifying the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Li'an is a procedure of mutual oaths that leads to separation; Abu Hanifa and Muhammad rule it a ba'in divorce, while Abu Yusuf holds it creates permanent prohibition.

This lesson examines the detailed procedure of li'an as established by the Quran and Sunnah, and then analyzes the disagreement within the Hanafi school on whether the resulting separation is a ba'in divorce or a permanent prohibition. Understanding both the ritual and the ikhtilaf is essential for applying this ruling correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Li'an is a legal procedure for a husband who accuses his wife of adultery without witnesses. The ruling is that it is a valid (sahih) procedure that necessitates separation after completion.
The procedure is an exception to the general rule that adultery requires four witnesses.
2
Locate the dalil
Both the Quran (Surah al-Nur 24:6-9) and authentic hadith (e.g., from Sa'id ibn Jubayr) establish the exact wording and order of the oaths.
The dalil is qati' al-thubut and qati' al-dalalah, so the ruling is firmly established.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The imperative verbs in the verses (e.g., 'فشهادة') indicate obligation, and the specification of four oaths plus the fifth shows the required format. The pointing gesture is derived from the demonstrative pronoun 'فيما رميتها'.
The wajh shows that the husband must point to the wife during his oaths to identify her.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
After the procedure, the judge separates the couple. Abu Hanifa and Muhammad hold it is a ba'in divorce. Abu Yusuf holds it creates a permanent prohibition (hurmah), forbidding remarriage.
The ikhtilaf is based on different interpretations of the hadith and the analogy to ila'.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad: ba'in divorce. This is because the majority of Hanafi scholars and the stronger evidence (analogy to ila' and the athar of Ibrahim al-Nakha'i) support it.
The tarjih authority is the later Hanafi consensus, though the author of Al-Sharh al-Thamiri presents both views.

ويشير اليها في جميع ذلك۔ مرو جب قسم کھائے تو اس وقت عورت کی طرف اشارہ کرے۔
کیونکہ عبارت میں ہے فیما رمیت ہے جس چیز کا میں نے اس کو تہمت ڈالا ، اس میں اشارہ استعمال کیا ہے نام نہیں لیا ہے۔ اس لئے انگلی سے عورت کی طرف اشارہ کرے تاکہ وہ عورت متعین ہو جائے۔

آیت اور حدیث دونوں میں اسی طرح لعان کرنے کا تذکرہ ہے۔ ويدروا عنها العذاب ان تشهد اربع شهادات بالله انه لمن الكاذبين والخامسة ان غضب الله عليها ان كان من الصادقين (آیت ۹ سورۃ النور ۲۴) اور حدیث میں ہے۔ عن سعيد بن جبير ... ثم ثنى بالمرأة فشهدت اربع شهادات بالله انه لمن الكاذبين والخامسة ان غضب الله عليها ان كان من الصادقين ثم فرق بينهما (مسلم شریف، کتاب اللعان ص ۴۸۸ نمبر ۱۴۹۳ ابو داؤد شریف ، باب فی اللعان ص ۳۱۳ نمبر ۲۲۵) اس آیت اور حدیث میں لعان کرنے کے طریقے کا تذکرہ ہے۔ اور یہ بھی ہے کہ عورت کہے اگر مرد تہمت میں سچا ہے تو مجھ پر غضب ہو۔
واذا التعنا فرق القاضي بينهما۔ دونوں کے لعان سے فارغ ہونے کے بعد قاضی دونوں کے درمیان تفریق کر دے۔
حدیث میں گزرا ثم فرق بينهما (مسلم شریف، کتاب اللعان ص ۲۸۸ نمبر ۱۴۹۳ / بخاری شریف، باب التفریق بین المتلاعنن ص ۸۰۱ نمبر ۵۳۱۳) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ لعان کے بعد قاضی خود بیوی شوہر کے درمیان تفریق کرادے۔
وكانت الفرقة تطليقة بائنة عند ابي حنيفة ومحمد وقال ابو يوسف تكون حرمة۔ طرفین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ جو فرقت شوہر کی حرکت سے ہو وہ طلاق بائنہ شمار کی جاتی ہے۔ جیسے ایلاء شوہر کی حرکت سے ہوتا ہے تو ایلاء طلاق بائنہ ہے اثر میں ہے۔ عن ابراهيم قال كل فرقة كانت من قبل الرجل فهى طلاق۔ اور اگلی روایت میں ہے۔ عن ابراهیم قال كل فرقة فهى تطليقة بائن (مصنف ابن ابي شيبة 9 من قال كل فرقة تطليقه ج رابع ، ص ۱۱۳ نمبر ۱۸۳۳۷) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ جو فرقت بھی شوہر کی جانب سے ہو وہ طلاق بائنہ شمار ہوگی۔ اور لعان شوہر کی جانب سے ہے اس لئے یہ بھی طلاق بائنہ شمار ہوگی۔ امام ابو یوسف کی دلیل یہ اثر ہے۔ قال سهل حضرت هذا عند رسول الله الله الله المضت السنة بعد في المتلاعنين ان يفرق بينهما ثم لا يجتمعان ابدا (ابوداؤد شریف، باب فی اللعان ص۳۱۳ نمبر ۲۲۵ رستن للبیہقی ، باب ستۃ اللعان و نفی الولد)
Book of Li'an: He testifies four times, saying each time: 'I testify by Allah that I am truthful in my accusation of adultery against her.' Then he says the fifth time: 'The curse of Allah be upon me if I am among the liars in my accusation of adultery against her.' And he points at her during all of that. Then the woman testifies four testimonies, saying each time: 'I testify by Allah that he is among the liars in his accusation of adultery against me.' And she says the fifth time: 'The wrath of Allah be upon me if he is among the truthful in his accusation of adultery against me.' When they have performed li'an, the judge separates them, and the separation is a ba'in divorce according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, while Abu Yusuf said it [results in] permanent prohibition.
The same manner of li'an is mentioned in the verse: 'And those who accuse their wives and have no witnesses except themselves, then the testimony of one of them is four testimonies by Allah that he is among the truthful, and the fifth that the curse of Allah be upon him if he is among the liars' (Surah al-Nur 24:6-7). This verse mentions the method of li'an, and also that the fifth [oath] is 'curse of Allah upon me if I am among the liars'. It also shows that li'an begins with the man, because he is the one who made the accusation. It is also mentioned in a hadith: from Sa'id ibn Jubayr... 'He began with the man, who testified four times by Allah that he is among the truthful, and the fifth that the curse of Allah be upon him if he is among the liars...' (Muslim, Kitab al-Li'an, p.488, no.1493; Abu Dawud, Bab fi al-Li'an, p.1313, no.2256/2253). This hadith shows the same method of li'an and that it begins with the man.
رمی: 'throwing an arrow', here meaning 'making an accusation of adultery'.
'And he points at her during all of that.' When he swears, he should point to the woman. Because the phrase 'فيما رميتها' uses a demonstrative pointing, not a name. So he should point to her with his finger so that the woman is identified.
'Then the woman testifies four testimonies...' After the man's testimony, the woman testifies four times: 'I make Allah my witness that he is lying in his accusation of adultery against me.' And the fifth time: 'The wrath of Allah be upon me if he is truthful in his accusation of adultery against me.'
Both the verse and hadith mention this method of li'an. 'And it [the punishment] is averted from her if she testifies four times by Allah that he is among the liars, and the fifth that the wrath of Allah be upon her if he is among the truthful' (Surah al-Nur 24:9). And in the hadith: from Sa'id ibn Jubayr... 'Then he turned to the woman, and she testified four times by Allah that he is among the liars, and the fifth that the wrath of Allah be upon her if he is among the truthful; then the judge separated them' (Muslim, p.488, no.1493; Abu Dawud, p.313, no.225). This verse and hadith mention the method of li'an, and also that the woman says: 'If the man is truthful in the accusation, then the wrath of Allah be upon me.'
'When they have performed li'an, the judge separates them.' After both have finished li'an, the judge separates them. A hadith mentions: 'then he separated between them' (Muslim, p.288, no.1493; Bukhari, Bab al-Tafriq bayn al-Mutala'inin, p.801, no.5313). This hadith shows that after li'an, the judge himself separates the husband and wife.
'And the separation is a ba'in divorce according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, while Abu Yusuf said it [results in] permanent prohibition.' The evidence of the two parties [Abu Hanifa and Muhammad] is that any separation that occurs due to the husband's action is considered a ba'in divorce, like Ila' (vow of abstention) which occurs by the husband's action is a ba'in divorce. There is an athar (tradition) from Ibrahim: 'Every separation that comes from the man is divorce.' And in another narration: 'Every separation is a ba'in divorce' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba). This athar shows that any separation from the husband is considered a ba'in divorce. And li'an is from the husband's side, so it will also be considered a ba'in divorce. The evidence of Abu Yusuf is this athar: Sahl said: 'I was present with the Messenger of Allah ﷺ during li'an. After that, the sunna regarding those who perform li'an was that they are separated and never come together again' (Abu Dawud, p.313, no.225; Bayhaqi).
Source pages p. 176

Commentary
This passage from Al-Sharh al-Thamiri discusses the procedure of li'an (mutual cursing) and its legal consequences. The passage type is a ruling with proof, as it cites both the Quran and Hadith to establish the method and effects of li'an.

The author first details the husband's testimony: he must swear four times by Allah that he is truthful in his accusation of adultery against his wife, and then a fifth time invoking Allah's curse on himself if he is lying. The wife then responds with four oaths that her husband is lying, and a fifth invoking Allah's wrath on herself if he is truthful. Both the Quran (Surah al-Nur 24:6-9) and authentic hadith (from Sa'id ibn Jubayr) are cited as evidence for this procedure.

A subtle point is that the husband must point to his wife during the oaths, as the Quran uses the demonstrative pronoun 'فيما رميتها' which indicates a pointing gesture, not a direct naming. This is to identify the specific woman being accused.

After both parties complete the li'an, the judge must separate them. This is based on the hadith that after the Prophet ﷺ performed li'an for a couple, he ordered their separation. The separation is a definitive legal effect of li'an.

The passage then discusses the nature of this separation. According to Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, the separation is a ba'in divorce (irrevocable divorce), meaning the husband cannot take his wife back without a new marriage. Their evidence is that any separation initiated by the husband's action (like ila') results in a ba'in divorce, and li'an is initiated by the husband's accusation. They cite the statement of Ibrahim al-Nakha'i: 'Every separation from the man is divorce.'

Imam Abu Yusuf differs and holds that the separation results in a permanent prohibition (hurmah), meaning the couple can never remarry. His evidence is the hadith of Sahl ibn Sa'd that the Prophet ﷺ said: 'the sunna regarding those who perform li'an is that they are separated and never come together again.' This hadith implies a complete and permanent severance, akin to three irrevocable divorces.

The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) in the Hanafi school is the view of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, that it is a ba'in divorce, allowing remarriage with a new contract if the wife did not actually commit adultery (as indicated by her oaths). However, if the wife confesses to adultery, the husband can still divorce her, but li'an would be unnecessary.

In summary, the passage establishes the precise wording and manner of li'an, the role of the judge in effecting separation, and the intra-madhhab dispute on whether the separation is a ba'in divorce or a permanent prohibition.

Key Terms
اللعان (al-li'ān): A mutual oath procedure between husband and wife when the husband accuses his wife of adultery without witnesses, involving four oaths each and a fifth oath of curse/wrath.
طلاق بائن (talāq bāʾin): An irrevocable divorce that ends the marriage immediately; the husband cannot take his wife back without a new marriage contract.
حرمة (ḥurmah): Permanent prohibition; after the separation, the couple is forever forbidden to remarry.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), what is the legal nature of the separation resulting from li'an?
A) A revocable divorce (talāq rajʿī)
B) A ba'in divorce (talāq bāʾin), allowing remarriage with a new contract
C) A permanent prohibition (ḥurmah), forbidding remarriage forever
D) No separation; the marriage continues

Key Takeaway
Li'an is a Quranically-mandated procedure of mutual oaths that results in judicial separation; the relied-upon Hanafi position is that this separation is a ba'in divorce, allowing remarriage with a new contract.

The Qadi Must Separate the Couple after Li'an
Ruling on separation after li'an with proof from hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that the qadi must separate the spouses after li'an and identify the hadith evidence that proves this obligation.

Core Idea
After li'an, the qadi must separate the couple — the Prophet's action is a binding command.

In this lesson, we examine the ruling that after the mutual imprecation procedure (li'an), the qadi is obligated to issue a separation (tafriq) between the spouses. The evidence comes directly from the Prophet ﷺ's practice in the famous li'an hadith. We will unpack the legal implications and address a common misunderstanding.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What exactly is being ruled upon? The qadi's separation of the spouses after li'an. What is the hukm level? It is wajib (obligatory).
2
Locate the dalil
The hadith of the Prophet where he separated the li'an couple, narrated in Muslim and Bukhari. The key phrase is 'thumma farraqa baynahuma' (then he separated between them).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does the hadith prove obligation? In Hanafi usul, the Prophet's action when accompanied by a statement or context indicating legislation is considered a command (amr) that indicates obligation (wujub).
The phrase is explicit: farraqa (he separated) is a past tense action, but the context of li'an shows it was a legal ruling.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some scholars, particularly the Shafi'i school, hold that the separation is not obligatory but merely permissible (ja'iz). They argue the Prophet's action does not necessarily indicate compulsion.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi position
The Hanafi school adheres to the apparent command and maintains that the qadi must separate without delay. This is the mufta bihi position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۲۰۶۷] (۹) جب دونوں لعان کرلیں تو قاضی تفریق کر دے۔
دونوں کے لعان سے فارغ ہونے کے بعد قاضی دونوں کے درمیان تفریق کر دے ۔
او پر حدیث میں گزرا ثم فرق بينهما (ج) (مسلم شریف، کتاب اللعان ص ۲۸۸ نمبر ۱۴۹۳ / بخاری شریف، باب التفریق بین المتلاعنین ص ۸۰۱ نمبر ۵۳۱۳) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ لعان کے بعد قاضی خود بیوی شوہر کے درمیان تفریق کرادے۔
[2067] (9) When both have performed li'an, the qadi should separate them. After both have finished li'an, the qadi should separate between them. It passed earlier in the hadith that he then separated between them. (Muslim, Kitab al-Li'an, p. 288, no. 1493; Bukhari, Bab al-Tafriq bayn al-Mutala'innayn, p. 801, no. 5313) From this hadith it is understood that after li'an, the qadi himself separates between husband and wife.
Source pages p. 177

Commentary
This passage states the ruling that after both spouses complete the procedure of li'an (mutual imprecation for accusing each other of adultery), the qadi must separate them. The proof is the hadith that after the Prophet performed li'an between a couple, he separated them. The term 'tafriq' (separation) is ordered by the qadi, not optional. This ruling is from the Zahir al-Riwayah.

Key Terms
لعان (li'an): A procedure where spouses swear oaths accusing each other of adultery or denying paternity, with five oaths each.
تفريق (tafriq): Judicial separation ordered by the qadi after li'an.
قاضي (qadi): The judge who presides over the li'an and orders separation.

Key Takeaway
The qadi must separate the spouses after li'an; this is a wajib ruling proven by the Prophet's action.

The Nature of Li'an Separation: Ba'in Divorce or Permanent Prohibition?
Intra-Hanafi dispute on li'an separation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the nature of separation after li'an, explain the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, and identify the mufta bihi ruling.

Core Idea
Li'an separation is a ba'in divorce, allowing remarriage, not a permanent prohibition.

In this lesson, we examine an important dispute within the Hanafi school itself: what is the legal nature of the separation that occurs after li'an (mutual imprecation)? Is it an irrevocable divorce that permits remarriage, or does it create a permanent ban? We will trace the evidence of both sides and see why the majority position of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad is relied upon.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi majority position
Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani rule that the separation is a ba'in (irrevocable) divorce.
This is the mufta bihi position.
2
Identify the opposing view
Abu Yusuf holds that the separation creates a permanent prohibition (tahrim mu'abbad), preventing ever remarrying.
Intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
3
Analyze the majority evidence
They cite the athar from Ibrahim: 'Every separation from the husband is a divorce' and analogize to ila'.
Qiyas on ila' supports the general principle.
4
Analyze Abu Yusuf's evidence
He relies on the hadith: 'They are separated and never reunite.'
The hadith is interpreted as barring cohabitation under the li'an, not permanent remarriage.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The majority view is relied upon; Abu Yusuf's position is considered a valid but less authoritative opinion.
Zahir al-riwayah supports ba'in divorce.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

حاشیہ : (الف) عورت سے سزا ہٹا لی جائے گی اگر چار مرتبہ گواہی دی کہ خدا کی قسم شوہر جھوٹا ہے، اور پانچویں مرتبہ یہ کہے کہ اللہ کی اس پر غضب ہوا اگر وہ سچا ہے (ب) پھر عورت کی طرف متوجہ ہوئے ، پس اس نے چار مرتبہ گواہی دی کہ خدا کی قسم وہ جھوٹوں میں سے ہے، اور پانچویں مرتبہ کہا کہ اسپر اللہ کا غضب ہوا گر وہ سچا ہو ۔ پھر دونوں کے درمیان تفریق کر دی گئی ( ج ) پھر میاں بیوی میں تفریق کر دی گئی (1) حضرت ابراہیم سے منقول ہے کہ ہر تفریق جو مرد کی جانب سے ہو وہ طلاق ہے۔ اور دوسری روایت میں ہے کہ ہر تفریق طلاق بائنہ ہے (ہ) حضرت سہل نے فرمایا میں حضور کے پاس لعان کے وقت حاضر ہوا۔ اس کے بعد لعان کرنے والوں میں سنت یہ رہی کہ دونوں میں تفریق کر دی جائے پھر بھی جمع نہ ہوں۔
[2068] (10) And the separation will be a ba'in divorce according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, and Abu Yusuf said it will be permanent prohibition. Their proof is that any separation arising from the husband's action is considered ba'in divorce, like Ila' (vow of abstinence) which is from the husband's action and is ba'in divorce. (2) There is an athar: from Ibrahim who said: Every separation that is from the husband is a divorce. And in another narration: from Ibrahim who said: Every separation is a ba'in divorce. (From Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, etc.) From this athar it is understood that any separation from the husband's side is counted as ba'in divorce. And li'an is from the husband's side, so this is also ba'in divorce. Abu Yusuf's proof is the athar: Sahl said: I was present with the Messenger of Allah, then the sunnah after him regarding those who perform li'an is that they are separated and never reunite. (Abu Dawud, Bab fi al-Li'an, p. 313, no. 225; Bayhaqi) Footnotes: (a) … (b) … (j) … (1) … (h) …
Source pages p. 177

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute. The issue is the legal nature of the separation after li'an. Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani rule that the separation is a ba'in (irrevocable) divorce, allowing remarriage after a new contract. Their evidence is the general principle that any separation originating from the husband is a divorce, analogizing to Ila'. They cite an athar from Ibrahim al-Nakha'i that every separation from the husband is a divorce, specifically a ba'in divorce. Abu Yusuf argues that the separation creates permanent prohibition (taḥrim mu'abbad), preventing ever remarrying. His proof is the practice of the Prophet and the Companions who separated the couple permanently, as reported by Sahl. The mufta bihi position is that of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad: ba'in divorce. The source of the hadith is given in the footnotes.

Key Terms
طلاق بائن (talaq ba'in): An irrevocable divorce that allows remarriage without a new contract.
تحريم مؤبد (tahrim mu'abbad): Permanent prohibition from ever marrying again.
إيلاء (ila'): A husband's vow to abstain from intercourse.
لعان (li'an): Mutual imprecation procedure when husband accuses wife of adultery without witnesses.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, what is the nature of the separation after li'an?
A) Permanent prohibition
B) Ba'in divorce
C) Raj'i divorce
D) Khul' divorce

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school primarily holds that li'an separation is a ba'in divorce, allowing remarriage, despite Abu Yusuf's view of permanent prohibition.

Permanent Prohibition After Li'an
Declares that li'an results in permanent marriage prohibition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that li'an results in a permanent marriage prohibition and distinguish it from temporary separations.

Core Idea
After li'an, spouses are forever forbidden to each other — a definitive and permanent dissolution.

This lesson examines the legal effect of li'an (mutual imprecation) on marriage according to the Hanafi school. The passage explicitly states that li'an creates a permanent prohibition (tahrim mu'abbad), meaning the spouses can never remarry. Understanding this ruling is crucial because it contrasts with some other schools that allow remarriage under certain conditions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is li'an — the mutual imprecation that occurs when a husband accuses his wife of adultery without witnesses. The ruling is that after li'an, the marriage becomes permanently unlawful.
The passage attributes this ruling to Imam Muhammad and Imam Abu Yusuf.
2
Understand the term 'tahrim mu'abbad'
The Arabic phrase 'tahriman mu'abbadan' means eternal prohibition. It indicates that the separation is absolute and cannot be reversed by any means.
This is a stronger effect than a revocable divorce (talaq raj'i) which allows remarriage during the waiting period.
3
Recognize the consequence for the spouses
The commentary explains that the wife and husband can never be reunited (kabhi nahi mil sakenge). This is the practical application of the permanent prohibition.
The permanence is based on the hadith that the Prophet (peace be upon him) separated the li'an couple and forbade their reunion.
4
Distinguish from other schools
Note that the Hanafi position is that this prohibition is permanent. Some other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) allow remarriage if the husband later admits to lying. This lesson focuses only on the Hanafi view as a ruling statement.
The cross-madhhab difference is a matter for later study; here we accept the matn.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب اللعان
محمد رحمهما الله وقال ابو يوسف رحمه الله يكون تحريما مؤبدا [۲۰۶۹ (۱۱) اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ لعان کے بعد بیوی شوہر کبھی نہیں مل سکیں گے۔ کیونکہ دونوں کے درمیان حرمت موبد ہوگئی۔
Book of Li'an. Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on him) said, and Abu Yusuf (may Allah have mercy on him) said: It becomes a permanent prohibition. [2069 (11)] From this it is understood that after li'an, the wife and husband can never be reunited. Because permanent unlawfulness has occurred between them.
Source pages p. 178

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the matn of Kitab al-Li'an. It states the Hanafi position, attributed specifically to Imam Muhammad and Abu Yusuf, that after the mutual imprecation (li'an) is completed, the marriage is permanently dissolved and the spouses can never remarry each other. The Urdu commentary emphasizes that this is an eternal prohibition (hurmah mu'abbadah), meaning it applies forever. The proof for this ruling is not explicitly quoted here but is based on the hadith of the Prophet (peace be upon him) who separated the li'an couple and forbade their reunion.

Key Terms
اللعان (al-li'an): Mutual imprecation between spouses when husband accuses wife of adultery without witnesses.
تحريما مؤبدا (tahriman mu'abbadan): Eternal prohibition; the spouses can never remarry after li'an.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the effect of li'an on the marriage according to Muhammad and Abu Yusuf?
A) The marriage is temporarily suspended for three months
B) The marriage is dissolved but they can remarry after a waiting period
C) The marriage becomes permanently prohibited; they can never remarry
D) The marriage remains valid but the husband must pay compensation

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school rules that li'an creates a permanent prohibition, so the spouses can never remarry.

Child Denial: Lineage Attached to Mother
Ruling that qadi negates child's lineage from father and attaches to mother

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that the qadi must negate the child's lineage from the father and attach it to the mother after li'an, and cite the hadith proof.

Core Idea
After li'an, the child's lineage is transferred from father to mother — a clear ruling based on prophetic practice.

In cases where a husband denies paternity of a child born during marriage, Islam provides a specific procedure: li'an. This passage presents the Hanafi ruling that the qadi must nullify the child's lineage from the father and instead attach the child to the mother. The proof is a hadith where the Prophet (peace be upon him) did exactly that. Let's walk through the legal operation of this ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the qadi required to do? The act is the qadi's judgment after li'an. The ruling is that it is obligatory (wajib) for the qadi to negate the child's lineage from the father and attach it to the mother.
Wajib here means obligatory for the qadi in his judicial capacity.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the hadith of Ibn Umar: the Prophet conducted li'an, the husband denied the child, then the Prophet separated them and attached the child to the woman.
This hadith is from Bukhari and Abu Dawud — it is a sunnah ahad but its meaning is clear.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The explicit action of the Prophet to attach the child to the mother after li'an demonstrates that this is the prescribed ruling. The ruling is derived from the prophetic act, which is a binding example.
The Hanafi school uses this as clear evidence (dalala qati).
4
Note the absence of ikhtilaf
The passage does not present any dispute. The Hanafi position is confirmed by the hadith, and this is the established ruling.
However, the cross-madhhab status is mukhtalaf fih regarding details like inheritance, but the core ruling is agreed.
5
Apply the ruling practically
After li'an, the child is no longer attributed to the father. The qadi declares the child belongs to the mother's lineage: the child is called by the mother's name and inherits from her and her relatives.
This affects birth records and inheritance distribution.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وان كان القذف بولد نفى القاضى نسبه والحقه بامه ۲۰۷۰ (۱) اول۔ اور اگر تہمت ہو بچے کی نفی کرنے کی تو قاضی اس کے نسب کی نفی کرے اور اس کو اس کی ماں کے ساتھ ملحق کرے۔ شوہر نے یوں کہا کہ یہ میرا بچہ نہیں ہے۔ اور بچے کی اپنے سے نفی کی تو لعان کے بعد قاضی بچے کا نسب باپ سے ساقط کر کے ماں کے ساتھ ملا دے گا۔ اور اب بچہ ماں کے ساتھ پکارا جائے گا باپ کے نام کے ساتھ نہیں۔ حدیث میں اس کا ثبوت ہے کہ آپ نے لعان کے بعد بچے کو ماں کے ساتھ ملحق کر دیا۔ عن ابن عمر ان النبي الله لاعن بين رجل وامرأته فانتفى من ولدها ففرق بينهما والحق الولد بالمرأة (الف) ( بخاری شریف ، باب ملحق الولد بالملاع ص ۸۰۱ نمبر ۳۱۵ ٫۵ابوداؤد شریف، باب فی اللعان ص ۱۳۱۳ نمبر (۲۲۵۹) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ تفریق کے بعد بچے کو ماں کے ساتھ ملحق کر دیگا۔
And if the accusation is regarding denying a child, the qadi negates his lineage and attaches him to his mother. 2070 (1) First: And if there is an accusation of denying a child, the qadi should negate his lineage and attach him to his mother. The husband said: 'This is not my child.' And he denied the child from himself, then after li'an, the qadi drops the child's lineage from the father and attaches him to the mother. Now the child will be called by the mother's name, not the father's. There is proof of this in the hadith that the Prophet (peace be upon him), after li'an, attached the child to the mother. From Ibn Umar: The Prophet (peace be upon him) conducted li'an between a man and his wife, and he denied her child, so he separated them and attached the child to the woman. (Bukhari, chapter: Attaching the child of the mula'an, p. 801, no. 5315; Abu Dawud, chapter on li'an, p. 1313, no. 2259). From this hadith it is understood that after separation, the child will be attached to the mother.
Source pages p. 178

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. It addresses the case where the husband accuses his wife of adultery by denying the paternity of her child. The Hanafi ruling is that the qadi (judge) must nullify the child's lineage from the father and instead attribute the child to the mother. The Urdu commentary explains the procedure: after li'an, the judge removes the child's lineage from the father, so the child is called by the mother's name, not the father's. The proof is the famous hadith of Ibn Umar where the Prophet (peace be upon him) performed li'an between a couple, the husband denied the child, then the Prophet separated them and attached the child to the mother. This is a clear evidence for the Hanafi position that after li'an, the child belongs to the mother's lineage.

Key Terms
نفي الولد (nafy al-walad): The husband's denial of paternity of a child born during marriage, requiring li'an.
الحاق بالام (ilhaq bi al-umm): Attaching the child's lineage to the mother after li'an.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
After li'an, the child's lineage is definitively transferred from the father to the mother based on prophetic practice.
